She stood and held out her hand. “Let’s go.”

 

Agatha gripped her hand and wasn’t sure how the other woman was going to pull her up wearing heels. Rio had no issue.

Chapter 14

Chapter Summary

Their date :) Did someone say.... Kareoke?! Long update enjoy!

CHAPTER 14

Agatha’s eyes took in the dark room with a multi-colored neon glow that accented the space well. Where were they? Her face stuck trying to take in the space. Rio moved to the counter to pay for something, picking up items as she came away with what looked like a green and purple ball. She handed the purple one to Agatha. “My lady.”

 

Agatha pursed her lips wondering what she was meant to do with this, when Rio grabbed her free hand. “We need to pick out our weapons…” 

 

Agatha’s mouth opened as she tried to form a coherent question but none came out. As she was dragged along, they made it to a stand that held different types of putters. Rio let go of her as she examined the devices, Agatha just grabbing the first one she saw. Rio’s appraisal seemed to take longer as her eye for these things seemed to be a bit technical.

 

Agatha tapped hers on the ground as she waited. “What are you, a connoisseur of golf sticks?”

 

Rio ignored her attitude and continued her search until she came upon the one she wanted. “I played golf growing up.” She cocked an eyebrow at her date. “Any fan of mine would know that.” She took a step towards Agatha sizing her up. “Did you lie about being a fan?” She looked her up and down. “Cause, I’m not going to lie, I could be into that.”

 

Agatha rolled her shoulders. “I know plenty about you. You are correct, anyone should remember that fact, you certainly talk about that interesting fact enough.” She sniffed. “I just… forgot.” She pursed her lips then when Rio only stared, her blue eyes rolled. “Your golfing abilities aren't my favorite thing about you, so sue me.”

 

Rio relaxed. “Hm, I’ll have to find some other way to impress you then, but I’m hopeful my game here does, at least a bit. I’ve got a wicked trick shot.” She winked. 

 

Agatha followed Rio as she moved to the first hole. The neon pinks, greens, and purples made the landscape feel foreign, like they had been transported to another world. And one thing Rio hadn’t exaggerated about was the fact that she was good, too good. She went out of her way to trick shot every single hole and Agatha had to admit, it was pretty impressive, even if she fought the way her facials were threatening to show it.

 

Agatha herself hated playing golf. She got frustrated and gave up on the first two holes but soon after that Rio took it upon herself to help. Her body coming up to mold to Agatha’s, her hands helping her grip the pole. “So you need to tighten your grip, but not too tight. Relax for me and just feel how I do it.”

 

Agatha’s breathing was heavy in her own ears as Rio guided her through a stroke. Her head grew dizzy with Rio’s warm body against her own. She had forgotten where they were and what they were doing when the ball sailed over the barriers and hit three points before dropping into the hole. Agatha’s eyes looked down at Rio’s hands in utter bewilderment. “I have no idea how you did that.”

 

Rio gripped her harder, her body pressing firmly into Agatha’s. “I can show you again, if you’d like?” Her voice dipped and promised of other things that were yet to come. 

 

Agatha released the putter, closing her eyes a moment later at the sound of the thing clattering to the floor. Blue eyes cringed at the noise in embarrassment. 

 

Rio bent to pick up the putter as she lightly tugged on Agatha’s wrist. “Let’s go grab a table and some snacks.” 

 

Agatha was left at a small table, taking in the designs in the cafe room. Her eyes watching the waves of colors, the lights rippling across the walls. Rio returned with three baskets and scooted into the seat across from her. “Okay, so I got cheese sticks, chicken nuggets and sliders.” She removed two soda’s from where she was holding them in her arm. Extending one root beer to Agatha.

 

The brunette smirked at the choices, she had never imagined that any point of tonight would be so down to earth. It was comforting. “Works for me.” She took her drink and opened it, taking a sip and relaxing, her fingers locating a cheese stick she started to eat, Rio quickly joining in.

 

Agatha’s eyes watched Rio, not quite sure how to figure her out. “So… I had to get dressed up, in expensive clothing, for this place?” She let her eyes land on Rio’s. “Or just for a date with you?” Her hand covered her mouth as she took another bite. “Not that I’m complaining, this is probably the best date I have been on in a long time.”

 

Rio shoved a chicken nugget into her mouth shaking her head before chewing slowly and swallowing. “It’s for where we are going after, this is just the dinner portion.”

 

Blue eyes widened. “There’s more to this date?”

 

Rio let her shoulder’s fall. “Unless… you didn’t want to do anything else?”

 

Agatha looked down at the table, frustrated that she didn’t know how to engage in such a delicate dance. Flirting during a first date was hard, not something she excelled at. And doing said date with a celebrity that constantly was giving her mild heart palpitations was another challenge entirely. “I didn’t say I wanted the night to end, I was… merely curious.”

 

Rio seemed to try and perk back up. “I have an in with a nightclub near your hotel, figured we would eat then go for a bit of dancing… would you… like that?” her voice sounded a bit uncertain at the end, as if she was worried she might not be sure of Agatha’s preferences. 

 

Agatha inclined her head. “Sure, that sounds fun.” She hadn’t been to a club in years, but she had enjoyed dancing when she was younger. She tried not to think about if she was about to embarrass herself. She continued to eat as she looked about the room, not sure what else to say, her mind feeling as if it was rushing to find questions, but she kept coming up blank. 

 

Rio watched Agatha like she was the most interesting thing in the room. More than satisfied to sit in the silence, but finding herself wanting to know more about the woman in front of her. “So washed up theater kid, huh?”

 

Agatha just about choked on her food. Coughing before Rio rubbed at her arm

 

“You okay?”

 

Agatha nodded as she finished the end of her coughing fit. “Yeah… I’m fine.”

 

Rio let her hand trail down to Agatha’s forearm that peaked out from her sleeve when she bent her arm, “I don’t know if you know this… but I started out in theater, too.”

 

Agatha snorted. “You don’t say?”

 

Rio nodded enthusiastically. Aware that they were playing up a bit of ignorance. “Yeah, I played Elphaba in my school's version of Wicked.” She added, then tacked on more information in a hushed tone. “I also scored big with Erin Meadows on opening night,” She inclined her head. “She played Glinda.”

 

Agatha’s eyes widened. “Okay, I knew about you doing Wicked, but I didn’t know about you banging the good witch.”

 

Rio swelled with pride. “See there are still some things you don’t know about me.” She leaned her chin on her fist. “Tell me something else I don’t know about you.”

 

Agatha let her eyes drift to where Rio was still drawing patterns on her arm. “I… my first play was Beauty and the Beast.” Rio smiled but Agatha rushed on. “I played the old hag.”

 

Rio’s eyes crinkled. “That’s fantastic.”

 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “I have a decent cackle.”

 

Rio’s hand moved to hold Agatha’s and play with her hands. “I would love to hear it sometime.”

 

Blue eyes narrowed. “You most certainly are never going to hear that.”

 

Rio shrugged. “We’ll see.”

 

***

 

Agatha and Rio walked hand in hand on the way to the club when Agatha’s feet slowed for a moment, her chest constricting. Rio’s dark eyes followed her gaze, reading the sign.

 

“Karaoke?” Rio asked intrigued. 

 

Agatha’s eyes looked back at Rio, not really sure why she had stopped herself. “I just… haven’t seen a place like this in a while is all.” Her eyes lingered on the windows that were covered in fun lights. “I used to be good at this.” She sighed before shaking her head. “I don’t know why I stopped, I’m sorry, I don’t need to relive my college days.” As she moved to continue on, Rio kept her feet grounded, pulling her back.

 

“Hm, alright then. I will say that I’m not the best at this, but I am willing to give it a go. Just, don’t make fun of me when I fail to hit the notes?”

 

Blue eyes looked back at the establishment. “We don’t have to go, Rio… you had a plan for tonight.”

 

Rio’s eyebrow raised in challenge. “And now we have a new one.” 

 

Agatha looked down the street then back at Rio. “We don’t have to…”

 

Rio moved to get the door and held it open for her. “Let’s go. Show me what you got, Harkness.”

 

***

 

Agatha’s fingers flipped through the booklet, taking in the newer songs, she at least knew some of them. Her eyes were trying to note at least three numbers she wanted to do. Rio leaned in close, looking over her shoulder, already too comfortable in her space. Which Agatha tried to pretend was fine, but she was freaking out. 

 

“I’ll do whatever songs you want.” Rio offered up. 

 

Agatha rolled her eyes, shifting slightly. “You have to choose too. I don’t even know what kind of music you listen to.”

 

Rio smiled. “Oh no! More secrets you’ll have to uncover. It’s almost like I’m a real person.” She mock gasped as she placed a hand to her own chest. 

 

Agatha snorted. “I still don’t know that this isn’t all a dream.” She felt as Rio slid her arm around her waist, leaning her body in close. 

 

“I’ll pick some Brittany. Keep it classic.” Her eyes continued to glance over the titles. “Does that work for you?”

 

Agatha forgot for a moment what they were doing when Rio’s warmth took over her senses, before the girl leaned away and ordered some more food and drinks. Agatha discretely shook herself out of her daze.

 

Rio smirked when the sake and snacks arrived, shrugging as if to say, you didn’t think I was going to do this sober, did you ?

 

Agatha plugged in the song list while Rio poured the drinks, music quickly filling the room as the two women moved to down a shot before they rushed to get singing. Agatha taking the lower part and Rio taking the higher one. Rio giggled when she messed up the words even though they were on the screen. She might have missed them because she had been looking at Agatha in her element. She would have rather just watched Agatha all night, using her voice to convey a practiced emotion – Rio could relate to feeling at home pretending. Though she was impressed with how genuine the words to the songs were when they left Agatha’s lips. 

 

When the song was over, they did another and another and before Rio knew what had happened, Agatha turned to her after the last song and started to kiss her. Rio’s eyes fell closed as Agatha held her firmly by the back of the neck. Rio loved that Agatha enjoyed taking charge. 

 

They made out for a good while before the room gave them a warning that their time was almost up, Agatha taking Rio’s hand and setting the course back to the hotel, with no room to mistake what she wanted.

 

When they entered the room Agatha slowed Rio down as she carefully took off the expensive clothing she wore. “Don’t want to mess these up, that way you can return them.”

 

Rio’s face fell. “Agatha, those were a gift. You’re taking them.”

 

Agatha shifted uncomfortably. “I don’t know how to explain where I got them from to my mother and my son.”

 

Rio shrugged. “Tell them that the training program requires clothing and that you got them from a friend.”

 

Agatha cleared her throat, her emotions a bit wired with the alcohol in her system. “I don’t have friends…not anymore,”

 

Rio moved forward, and moved Agatha’s hair out of her face. “I’m your friend.”

 

Agatha didn’t know what to do with Rio’s kindness so she took control of the situation before Rio could say anything else even remotely sentimental, and smashed her lips into the other woman’s.

Chapter 15

Chapter Summary

Nicky gets sick... the same kid Rio was never going to meet...

CHAPTER 15

Agatha jolted awake as her phone started ringing. She frantically escaped Rio’s arms to locate it and as she did she felt her breath catch in her throat. “Nicky?”

 

She heard her mother sigh and she squatted to the floor closing her eyes, feeling off balance. “Mother?”

 

Evanora clicked her jaw. “Nicky’s sick. You need to come home, now . I am doing what I can, but this filth you’ve allowed into his soul is hard to clean and it’s rotting him from the inside out.”

 

Agatha rubbed at her forehead. “H-has he thrown up?”

 

She heard her mother grumbling. “Of course the child has, didn’t I say he was ill? Honestly, Agatha, you didn’t get your lack of brains from me. Why weren’t you up already? It’s nearly eight in the morning...”

 

Agatha felt soft hands rub at her back, her body relaxing, if only a bit. “I’ll head home right away.” Her breath hitched as the call went dead. She felt a warm body encasing her fragile form.

 

Rio’s voice was soft as she inquired. “Is Nicky okay?”

 

Agatha shook her head, not quite present. “I… I shouldn’t have left him.”

 

Rio took a deep breath and let it out slowly. “You can’t always be there, Agatha.”

 

The woman shook her head. “I… I need to get home.”

 

Rio caught her chin and turned it towards her. “Can you drive, right now?”

 

Agatha’s mouth opened and closed before she could land on her response. Finally locating one. “I’m going to have to.”

 

Rio shook her head. “I’ll drive you, then get a taxi back,”

 

Agatha bit her lip. “I can’t ask you to do that.”

 

Rio shrugged, “You're not. Don’t worry, it’s not like I am trying to meet your kid, I’ll be discreet. We should stop and get him a few things on the way, I know I hate feeling sick. I’ve got a few tricks up my sleeve for a quick recovery.”

***

 

Rio had driven while Agatha slept. The other woman knocked out quickly the moment they got settled in the car. Rio tried not to watch Agatha dream, but occasionally her eyes darted over to take in the woman curled up against the window. She couldn’t help it. Rio’s eyes tried to stick close to her phone as she navigated to Agatha’s hometown. When she was about fifteen minutes away, she pulled off the road to stop at a pharmacy. She had just taken off her seatbelt when Agatha woke up, hitting the window.

 

“What?” She looked around her as if she didn’t know where she was, her eyes doing a double take when Rio was sitting in her driver's seat. The dark haired woman pointed at the store.

 

“I was just going to run in real quick and get Nicky a few things…”

 

Agatha, looked around then back at Rio shaking her head, her anxieties seemed to be rushing back now that she was conscious. “No… I need to get home.”

 

Rio’s eyes slid to the store, noting the brunette’s panic. “I guess… I can drop you off, then go get a few things.”

 

Agatha ran a hand through her hair, readying herself to plead. “Nicky… he needs me,”

 

Rio put her seatbelt back on and started to back out of the parking space. “Okay, I got it. I’m sorry, I misunderstood. You’re right. Let’s get him his mom, I’m sure that will help him feel better.”

 

***

 

When they arrived at Evanora’s house, an old woman with wavy silver hair stood glaring from the doorway in a burgundy cloak. Rio blatantly ignored the tension as she followed Agatha in.

 

Evanora snarled as her daughter entered the home. “Was there even a job interview?” Eyeing Rio as if she were wearing something provocative and not her simple sweats. 

 

Agatha opened her mouth when Rio placed a hand on her back, inquiring softly about what mattered at the moment. “Nicky?”

 

Agatha shook her head and took a step back from Rio, her eyes not leaving Rio’s steady brown gaze. “Mom, is Nicky upstairs?”

 

Evanora grunted and Agatha took off up the stairs. Her feet quickly took her to her child. Rio kept at a slower pace behind her and saw the moment the boy came into view. He was sitting in a large bed, blankets piled high and pillows behind his back. His eyes lidded. “Momma?” 

Upon further inspection, the child’s skin looked too pale, his eyes glassy. Rio’s fingers pressed at her own chest as it ached. 

 

Agatha sat gingerly on the bed next to him. “Nicky, I am so sorry I wasn’t here.” She wrapped her arms around him. “What hurts, baby?”

 

Nicky wrapped his arms back around her. He groaned. “Everything. I threw up.”

 

Agatha started to run her hands through his short hair, clearly forgetting it wasn’t longer anymore, as her fingers hovered in the air.

 

Rio stood silently by, watching this woman do her mom thing. Rio took in Nicky’s pale skin with worry and cleared her throat, announcing herself. “Hey kid, how much did you throw up?”

 

Nicky’s eyes lifted, his eyebrows furrowing as if he hadn’t noticed there was another person in the room yet. He tilted his head but answered. “A few times…”

 

Rio tried to smile. “Well, that’s not good.” She turned her attention to Agatha. “We should take him to get checked out. I am sure he at least could use some fluids,” Her dark eyes watched as Agatha hesitated, clearly uncomfortable with the idea. Her body, tightening, but before she could protest she bit her cheek and nodded. 

 

Agatha’s eyes found Rio’s, “Could… could you sit with him a second while I… find his insurance card?”

 

Rio tried to offer up a smile but she wasn’t sure that it was comforting in any way. “Sure. I don’t mind.” Agatha’s face was so upset Rio knew she worried she would say no. Rio indicated quickly that she would do as asked, nodding her head.

 

Agatha leaned forward and kissed Nicky’s hair as she stood. “This is… my friend, Nicky, she’s going to stay with you for a moment.” The little boy nodded and Agatha weaved around Rio, her footsteps thundering down the hall as she frantically disappeared.

 

Rio took a step towards Nicky, “Hey, I’m Rio. Is it okay if I sit next to you, or would you prefer I stay over here?”

 

The little boy looked down and shrugged before he patted the space next to him, Rio sliding in next to him and taking out her phone a moment later. “Do you like games? Or is there something you wanna watch?”

 

The little boy smiled and took her phone, starting to flip through the apps he leaned against her, causing Rio’s heart to seize in her chest. This was the kid she was never going to meet, that fact felt like a warning sign was flashing in her fucking face. She tried to keep breathing, she leaned her arm across his back as she settled in to watch a game the boy had opened and started playing. The sounds and movements helping keep her calm. It wasn’t a big deal, she was just keeping him company, this was just one time, then she was never going to see him again. She could do this.

 

Agatha returned a few moments later panting as she now had her purse and a medical card gripped tightly in her hand. “We should go.”

 

Rio nodded. Standing as she noticed Nicky’s hand lifted to his head as he tried to move. She leaned forward and scooped him up, the kid wrapping his arms around her neck, his head buried into her. Blue eyes grew large as she tried to step forward to take her six year old son, when Rio shook her head.

 

“I can carry him. I work out.”

 

Agatha looked like she wanted to protest but gave in instead, leading the way back to the car. Rio opened the door and set the kid in gently. When Nicky placed his hand over his mouth, she slid in and grabbed a plastic bag from the ground, just in time, before his face tipped forward into the bag and he vomited. His whole body heaving, before the shivering started.

 

Rio helped him hold the bag, before taking one hand to help him fix his seat belt. Her eyes lifted. “Agatha, I got this, drive.”

 

Blue eyes looked towards the wheel as she turned the key and the car roared to life. 

 

***

 

The urgent care had been a just down the road, luckily it wasn’t too busy and they were put back into a room right away. The doctor came in to ask questions about what was going on. Agatha chewed at her lips as she took breaks between her answers.

 

“He’s been unable to stop vomiting…” Her body was shaking, but not so gently that Rio didn’t notice. The woman silently helped her sit down besides Nicky, before speaking herself.

 

“We need some IV fluids with electrolytes, he can’t keep anything down. Maybe some anti nausea meds? Also, I think we’ll be wanting a full blood panel.”

 

Agatha’s eyes looked to the ground like she was going to be sick herself. The doctor simply nodded at the routine request. 

 

“We’ll need to place an IV. But none of this should take too long. The man leaned on his knees before taking a lollipop from his jacket and giving it to the boy. “Here, save this for later when you are feeling better, I have a feeling you’re a very brave boy and you’re going to do awesome today.”

 

Nicky took the lollipop and handed it to his mother. “Thank you.” He said to the doctor quietly, while his eyes looked to his Mom, wanting to know how badly everything was going to hurt.


While the nurse appeared and started to get set up, Rio watched as Nicky eyed the tools. Rio stepped in to disrupt his line of sight. “So, Nicky… I do this thing sometimes at hospitals. I’m like… the hospital witch.”

 

Nicky’s eyes looked up and for a moment, the child seemed distracted. “What’s a hospital witch?”

 

Rio clasped her hands and looked around her real quick to see how long the nurse might need to get ready, gauging the amount of time the child needed to be entertained for. “Well, I grant wishes to brave little kids. You get to wish for something that you really want and if you’re really brave, you get your wish.”

 

Nicky’s eyes seemed to come a little more into focus as he struggled to push his brain to think. “Anything I want?”

 

Agatha shook her head as if waking up. “Nicky.”

 

Rio smiled at the kid nodding. “Basically.”

 

The boy tapped his finger to his chin as his eyes shot back to her. “A puppy?”

 

Agatha’s eyes just about popped out of her head as she shook her head at Rio over her son.

 

Rio tried to school her features. “A puppy is sort of hard to come by, it could take a long while for me to locate one… is there anything from the store?”

 

Nicky seemed to think harder. “Well, if Momma goes away again, it would be good to be able to talk to her… without getting in trouble.” He looked at his mom briefly. “Do they still have iPads in the store?”

 

Rio didn’t look at Agatha as she nodded. “Sure they do, if you are really brave, we can grant your wish after today.”

 

Nicky’s eyes lit up, his face setting into a look of determination, his eyes locking with Rio’s. “I’m going to be so brave, you just watch.”

 

Rio smiled and kept her eyes far from Agatha’s gaze, she could already feel the frustration wafting off of her. She figured Agatha could set rules down about the device, what was the harm in her getting it for the boy if it made today, and future trips Agatha might take, easier on him?

 

Rio moved as the nurse scooted her rollie chair closer. “Okay, Nicolas, we’re going to place this thing in your arm real quick. It will hurt but only for a few moments. We’ll use this heat pack to relax your arm and get a good vein then we will place this ice to relax your arm when we’re done with our tests. You ready?”

 

Nicky’s little pale face nodded. His eyes drifted to Rio’s as the woman took his arm. Rio inclined her head. “Keep breathing, Nicky.” Dark eyes lifted and watched as Agatha’s grip on Nicky tightened.

 

The boy's eyes widened as he grunted. “Ow.” He looked down at the plastic in his arm and bit his lip. The nurse moved efficiently. 

 

“Good job, that’s done. Here’s the heat pack. Hold that there while I take some blood.” Nicky’s hands took the pack and quickly held it to his arm, his brows releasing slightly as the sting faded a little. 

 

Rio crossed her arms. “That was pretty badass little dude. Not even one tear?”

 

Nicky smirked. “Nope.”

 

Rio lifted her fist out and the kid bumped it. “Cool.”

 

Agatha watched as Nicky’s arm was hooked up to an IV drip and the nurse finished up. “Ok that is going to go for about forty minutes. Then we should be able to get you out of here.” Her eyes lifted to Agatha, “You’ll get an email about the results within a day. If there’s an issue you can follow up with his normal doctor or bring him back.” 

 

Agatha nodded her understanding as the woman snuck Nicky a hot wheels sticker and left. Nicky handed his mother the ice pack. “I wanna keep using the heat pack, this is cold.”

 

Rio took off her jacket and placed it around Nicky’s shoulders. The little boy smiled up at her. “Can I keep playing that game on your phone?”

 

Agatha went to shake her head when Rio handed over her cell phone. “You got it.” Messing the little boy’s hair a bit as she teased him. He took the phone in his hands and became engrossed in the activities.

 

Agatha’s hands shaking as she released her son. “I should… go deal with the bill. Can you?” She indicated her son with her gaze and Rio nodded. “Of course.” The older woman slipped out of the room.

 

Rio sat with Nicky watching him play when it seemed like Agatha was gone for a while. The little boy spoke as if he heard her thoughts. “Momma isn’t leaving me forever, is she?”

 

Rio’s concerned gaze returned to the boy in front of her. “Nicky, why would you think that?”

 

His little shoulders shrugged as he didn’t look away from the phone. “Mommy did.”

 

Rio felt the bile want to come up her throat, but she tapped it down. “Well, your Momma is not her.” She felt as Nicky leaned into her once more. “Okay.”

 

Rio ran her hand through his hair, the child sighing softly. Rio’s eyes taking into account that over half the IV bag was empty. “Are you feeling any better?”

 

Nicky nodded. “Yeah, I’m hungry.”

 

Rio chuckled. “Okay, well why don’t I go find your Momma and we get going soon so we can feed you?” Nicky smiled and looked up at her. “Can I pick lunch?”

 

Rio flashed her eyes at him. “Sure.” He giggled and she left him with her phone, taking note of the room number as she wandered back towards the front desk, her face scrunching as she heard Agatha’s voice frantic on the phone. 

 

“What do you mean you won’t cover the blood test?” She groaned quietly, muffling her voice, “He’s sick, it’s needed to rule out if it’s something serious… I just talked to that department…” She sounded like she was on the verge of tears. “What is the point in this stupid insurance if it forces me into poverty when I need to use it?”

 

Rio approached and reached out light fingers to touch Agatha’s shoulder, the woman flinching away from her, not knowing who was touching her. Rio stepped back as if burned. Her eyes lifting to the staff that were throwing pitiful looks Agatha’s way. Rio sighed and walked up to the desk speaking softly.

 

“How much does she owe?”

 

The woman let her gaze look towards the mother on the phone before Rio tried again. “I’m going to pay it for her.”

 

The woman let her shoulders relax. “It’s $522.” Rio nodded then produced a card discreetly. “Here.” She kept her voice low. “If we can get a receipt, we'll file with the insurance later.”

 

The woman nodded, running the card and printing a receipt. “I included the claim codes, I hope that helps her.” Rio nodded as the woman took a deep breath. “I know this is inappropriate…”

 

Rio’s eyes looked between Agatha still on the phone and the woman at the desk. Her face was tense. “What is it?”

 

She looked off towards the front doors. “Is there any way I could get your autograph? And you can totally say no…”

 

Rio sighed, smiling softly. Normally this would frustrate her, but the fact that things were so quiet and that they were the only people in the waiting room eased her mood. “I suppose I could do that real quick, just don’t be telling anyone else I’m here, alright?” She lifted an eyebrow and the woman broke out into a smile. “Oh, I won't, I'll keep it real hush hush.”

 

Rio took the offered paper and pen and glanced at the woman’s name plate writing a quick note. “Thanks for helping us today.” She handed the paper over as the next patient came through the doors, approaching the line to speak with the desk. The woman held out the paperwork for Rio, indicating to give it to Agatha. Rio took it with a quiet thank yo u before she wandered back over to her friend.

 

“Agatha, we should probably get back to Nicky.” Rio spoke softly. 

 

Blue eyes lifted to her as her voice cracked. “I need to figure out how to … pay for this.”

 

Rio handed her the receipt and paperwork and Agatha’s hand with the phone lowered, the insurance agent still making their excuses down the line, none the wiser that Agatha was no longer listening. “What?”

 

Rio took her free hand. “Let’s get back to Nicky. She put the codes on there to fight the insurance on this later. It wasn’t a big deal, I wanted Nicky to have the blood tests.”

 

Agatha followed blindly as Rio guided them back to the room, Nicky’s face lighting up the moment he saw both of them, color finally back in his cheeks.

 

***

 

Nicky practically jumped out of the car the moment it stopped moving. Agatha shouted. “Nicky, don't run!” She rolled her eyes. “You would have never known two hours ago he was on death’s door.”

 

Rio shrugged. “Fluids can do a lot, I’m glad he’s feeling better.”

 

Agatha’s hands gripped the steering wheel. “You didn’t need to run into the store on the way back.”

 

Rio lifted the bag. “He needed this stuff, he’s had a rough day.”

 

Agatha closed her eyes. “Don’t get him the iPad.”

 

Rio’s hand fell. “Agatha, he was brave today…”

 

Agatha’s eyes cut to her. “You need to stop,”

 

Rio felt her stomach drop. “Stop, what, Agatha?”

 

The woman shook her head angrily. “You should go.”

 

Rio bit her lip. “Yeah… I know. I’ll just… call a ride.”

 

Agatha’s hands slid to the bottom of the steering wheel. As she tried to even out her breathing. She managed a quiet, thank you after a moment.

 

Rio folded her hair behind her own ear. “Of course.” 

 

Agatha’s blue eyes took her in when she thought she wasn’t looking, as if she was trying to memorize her face up close. Rio wanted to ask when they would meet again but Agatha’s words had seemed so final. Agatha didn’t ask her to get out of the car and they sat there in silence until Rio’s ride she had ordered arrived. As she went to exit the car she heard Agatha quietly speak, almost too quiet to hear. 

 

“Let me know when you get home safe.”

 

She nodded and closed the door.

Chapter 16

Chapter Summary

Rio gets some news... and makes a counter offer and finds an excuse to reach out to Agatha.

Agatha finds her creativity again. Washed up theater kid who?

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

CHAPTER 16

 

Rio spent the rest of the day researching the ins and outs of iPads. She had noted Agatha’s address and while she had seemed embarrassed about Rio buying her son a gift, the kid had been brave, and made a good point of needing the device.

 

She input Agatha’s address and hit purchase, it would be delivered within a day. And if Agatha really didn’t want him having it, she could deal with that herself. Before she could move on from her phone, she saw a text from Billy mentioning that Agatha was trying to send her money back. Rio rolled her eyes.

 

Decline her offer.

 

She sighed as she looked up and saw that they were approaching her home, her eyebrow lifting as Lilia’s car sat out front. Lilia was watching Ruffland but she had taken him to her home, why were they back at Rio’s already? She was going to pick him up tomorrow as it was getting late.

 

She grabbed her suitcase, thanking the man as she took off towards her gate, inputting the code it clicked and she walked through, her suitcase needing to be yanked over the threshold. She made sure the gate secured itself then wandered to her front door. Her eyes rolled as it was already unlocked. Benny and Ruffland tore across the house barking up a storm as she smiled at their antics.

 

“Hey psychos.” 

 

Benny acted like he didn’t remember her for a second, before he sniffed her. Her baby in contrast, instantly sat at her feet, prancing like he really wanted to jump up on her, but knew better… while they had company.

 

She leaned forward and petted them both before ditching her bags in the main hall, she could unpack later. She walked back towards the kitchen and found Lilia sitting at the table on her laptop. 

 

“One moment, kiddo.” Lilia continued typing. 

 

Rio moved to the fridge and got herself a drink. Her hand gripping the top of the can as she moved to sit across from Lilia. The woman finished what she was doing then closed her laptop, leaning forward. 

 

“I have news.”

 

Rio shifted uncomfortably in her seat. “You didn’t contact me all weekend…”

 

Lilia waved her off. “I knew you were taking some personal time. How did that go?”

 

Rio shrugged, her face sullen, Lilia’s lips dipped downward as well. “Oh, Rio. I’m sorry. Was it the NDA? Did she not want to sign it?”

 

Rio leaned her head on her hand and shrugged. “No, she signed that.”

 

Lilia looked about, as if trying to decipher what had happened. “She didn’t think you were enough like your characters?”

 

Rio shook her head. “No… she seemed cool with it just being me. Well,” her eyes looked off to the side in thought. “After her panic attack.”

 

Lilia leaned forward and patted her arm. “I’m sorry.”

 

Rio bit her cheek. “I met her kid, it was a bit fast. I think she didn’t like that.”

 

Lilia squeezed her arm. “Look, you’re a good kid. You’re human, there aren’t rules for these things. Some people just don’t remember you’re just a person too.”

 

Rio’s eyes watered as she sniffed. “I’m not ready to talk about her. It's… fresh.”

 

Her mentor hummed. “That is fine, because in a moment, you won’t even remember this weekend.”

 

Rio’s eyes lifted skeptically. “Why?”

 

Lilia’s face broke out into a shit eating grin. “This is why I came by.”

 

Rio sat up straight. “You met with Sharon?”

 

Lilia nodded, trying to keep herself from bursting with the news, “I did!”

 

Rio felt like she was going to pass out. “And? Is the script good?”

 

Lilia smirked. “It’s more than good, baby. It’s barrier breaking.”

 

Rio leaned closer, her hand reaching for the laptop. “Well, I should prepare for the reading…”

 

Lilia trapped her hand on the table. “She asked me what it would take to get you on the project. They won’t be taking no for an answer.” She just about screamed. “You did it, Rio! You landed a Monument Pictures role!”

 

Rio’s hand covered her mouth as the tears came. “No…”

She rubbed at her face as Lilia navigated around the table, ready to wrap her arms around her, Rio standing and launching into the embrace.

 

“What the fuck!”

 

Lilia giggled. “I know!”

 

Rio shook and suddenly Ruffland was headbutting her hard. Her eyes looked down at his worried face. “It’s… a happy panic, dude, I promise.” 

 

Lilia released her and indicated the floor. “Let him do his job.”

 

Rio sat down carefully, using her dog to get to the floor, then once she was settled Ruffland plopped into her lap and scooted back into her chest. Rio wrapped her arms around him and placed her face in his soft fur as she tried to breathe.

 

Rio heard Lilia return to her laptop. “It’s a show about witches, queer witches.”

 

Rio snuggled closer to her dog as she continued to listen.

 

“The only hiccup is they're struggling to find someone to play your costar and love interest.” Rio’s head lifted slowly. Her mind starting to dissect the details.

 

Lilia had said they had to have her. Could she make a counter offer?

 

She cleared the emotions from her voice, “I want something.”

 

Lilia’s fingers stopped. “What?”

 

Rio sighed. “They said they had to have me. I want… to pick my costar.”

 

Lilia about shit herself, her tone turning to scold the younger girl. “Rio!”

 

Rio shrugged. “It’s a counter offer…”

 

Lilia groaned. “Do not mess this up for us, Rio.”

 

She turned her best puppy dog eyes on Lilia. “It’s just a request… they can say no…”

 

Lilia grumbled. “They can also decide they don’t want you as badly as they thought they did, at just the drop of a hat…”

 

Rio took a breath. “She’s good, Lilia, I’ve seen a small glimpse of her playing with her emotions, she’ll do good work.”

 

The woman leveled her gaze. “Who?”

 

Rio felt a little sick. “Agatha Harkness.”

 

Lilia’s brows raised. “Who the fuck is Agatha Harkness? ”

 

***

 

Sharon had wanted a self tape of this mysterious unknown that Rio wanted to work with. Rio had pondered for days how to reach out to Agatha again. She hadn’t heard anything further from the woman since she had left, though she had confirmation that the iPad was delivered.

 

She opened her messages with @downyourroad and felt her body tighten with anticipation of reaching out. She sighed. She knew this wouldn’t be an easy sell, and that nothing was guaranteed, but if there was even a chance at getting Agatha out of her situation, and closer to Rio, then she needed to at least try.

 

She typed a message.

 

@RioVidalsWhore69: I made it home. 

 

She watched as the message was instantly read.

 

@downyourroad: days later?

 

Rio rolled her eyes. Fine so she was pissed. So she didn’t message her right away, she had been busy since she got back. Negotiations with Monument took a second, especially if you were stupid enough to actually come back with terms.

 

@RioVidalsWhore69: I was busy. I’m sorry, about the late message. 

 

She watched as Agatha started and stopped typing a few times.

 

@downyourroad: My son wanted to thank the hospital witch. I tried to return the gift, but there was no way to give it back, apparently.

 

Rio smiled.

@RioVidalsWhore69: He deserved it. It was a present, so he could talk to you without stealing your computer.

 

@downyourroad: So it was a selfish gift?

 

Rio rolled her eyes.

 

@RioVidalsWhore19: whatever helps you sleep at night.

 

She practically felt the other woman huffing from across the internet.

 

@downyourroad: My son hasn’t stopped talking about you. 

 

Rio smiled a little at that. She had never thought she was good with kids, but Nicky was different, he was easy to talk to, even when he was sick.

 

@RioVidalsWhore69: He’s a good kid. I was glad he was feeling better. Speaking of, did you ever get the results?

 

She wondered if she was pushing too much, but apparently inquiring after Nicky was the right thing to say.

 

@downyourroad: He has a few numbers we need to follow up on, but ultimately he is doing alright now. 

 

Rio bit her lip at that concern she felt, but moved to continue on.

 

@RioVialsWhore69: I’m glad he’s relatively okay. Not to change the conversation, but I needed to talk to you. Do you think we could hop on a phone call?

 

She saw as her message was read and then how nothing came. She blew out a breath. Okay, so Agatha was going to be difficult today.

 

She moved to make herself coffee and by the time she was done her phone was beeping with an alert.

 

@downyourroad: I tried to send the money back. If you didn’t accept it, that’s on you. I’m not able to stop my whole life for you, until you figure out what you want.

 

Rio’s eyes narrowed…”What I want?”

 

She sent back her number, and waited.

 

She had to hand it to Agatha; she really knew how to stonewall her. She moved to her couch and turned on her tv, assuming she wouldn’t be hearing back from Agatha for a while when her phone chirped.

 

@downyouroad: You’re reckless. 

 

Rio smirked as she sent back a juvenile reply.

 

@RioVidalsWhore69: You’re reckless.

 

Her phone instantly started vibrating in her hand as she answered.

 

“Hey.”

 

She heard Agatha huff on the other end. “Well, what did you want from me?”

 

Rio rolled her eyes. “It’s nothing bad, Agatha, relax.”

 

“I signed your stupid paper, what did you do? Lose it?”

 

Rio laid down. “No. I filed it with Lilia.” Her eyes drifted to the tv. “Why? Were you planning on doing a tell all interview? Sign a book deal?”

 

She smiled as she heard Agatha scoff. “Please.”

 

Rio played with a piece of her hair. Her voice showed a rare dip into vulnerability. “It wouldn’t be the first time it’s happened to me.”

 

She heard the other woman let out a sigh. “Well, too bad I signed that paper then. Anyway, if it’s not about that, then why did you want me to call?”

 

Rio rubbed at the tattoo behind her ear, its presence a reminder of strength, bringing her the comfort she needed right now. She was feeling raw. “Am I not allowed to miss you?”

 

Agatha’s voice was firm. “No.”

 

Rio snorted. “I don’t think you get to make those decisions for me.” She moved forward before they could continue arguing. “Anyway, I have a proposition for you.”

 

She heard the other woman practically deflate. Her voice was careful. “Okay…”

 

Rio closed her eyes. “I need you to read for a role.” She opened one eye to look at the phone to see if it were disconnected, the clock was still running, staring her back in the face.

 

Agatha’s voice was hard. “What?”

 

Rio licked her lips. “Look. I… I saw how you can play with your emotions, the night at the karaoke bar. You’re decently good. There’s this role…”

 

Agatha barked out a laugh. “No.”

 

Rio tried again. “It’s just a self-tape.”

 

Agatha ground out her words. “I shouldn’t have told you anything about me.”

 

Rio tried to center herself, rubbing at her forehead. “Agatha, do you even know why you are so angry with me?”

 

She heard the other woman grunt. “Yes.”

 

Rio snorted. “Alright, then. Let me have it. What did I do?”

 

Agatha gasped. “Well, if you don’t know, then I’m not going to explain it to you.”

 

Rio closed her eyes again thinking through the weekend. “Was it because I ordered Nicky a blood test? Because I paid for that. I just wanted to make sure he was fully checked out…”

 

Agatha made a sound that appeared to be a poor attempt to cover up a quiet sob. “No… no, I’m not… mad about that.”

 

Rio pulled her knees up to her chest. “I’m sorry. For whatever I did.”

 

Agatha’s breathing was all she heard for a time after that. She let herself listen to the sound and tried to feel comforted by the fact that the woman was still on the phone with her. “Hey, look, it’s a good role, and it’s not like you would have to take it if by some miracle they offered it to you. But you’re good, Agatha, I don’t mind throwing a few auditions your way if it would help you and Nicky move on…”

 

Agatha gasped, sounding like she was growing angry. “Stop.”

 

Rio sighed. “Agatha. I’m not trying to hurt you. It’s just one video. It’s a short scene. I just need you to read for it. I won’t even watch the video, we can pretend no one ever will if that’s what you want. I just… have a good feeling about this.”

 

She was quiet as she listened to the sounds of Agatha sobbing. Her heart was pinching. She tried to find more words for the woman, but found her mind had gone blank. After a while she heard Agatha disconnect the call. Her fingers itching to say something else, but not knowing what wouldn’t make it worse. 

 

In the end, she sent the script. Turning off her phone, she went to take Ruffland for a walk.

 

***

 

Agatha’s eyes burned. Why would Rio send her a script? She didn’t have any experience, she had a college degree. She shook her head. She shouldn't look at it, that part of her, the creative part, died a long time ago. When she had met her wife, and that woman had hated that she wanted to be an actor and a writer. She hugged herself, hoping to stop the creeping prickling feelings that crawled up her spine when she thought of how calculating and manipulative her ex was. 

 

She had been told she sucked, that her emotions appeared false, even her real ones. She shook her head. What had Rio thought she had seen in her?

 

Her fingers inched back over to her phone, opening the script. The words that were seemingly random at first, clicked and suddenly they were jumping off the page when she finished the excerpt. She knew nothing about the character and yet, with this brilliant writing, she felt she knew her intimately. She found that she wanted to know her story.

 

She looked around the room. She wasn’t going to do this… but if she did… where could she even film?

 

Nicky came bounding down the stairs. His bright smile now firmly back in place as he had fully recovered from his illness. “Hey, Mom!”

 

Agatha smiled for his sake, even though she felt like vomiting. 

 

“Nicky. I got… another interview.”

 

The boy paused. “Oh…” He tried to smile. “Well, that’s great!”

 

She looked down at her phone then back at him. “They need me to do it today… do you think… that you could distract grandma for a while?” She felt pride swell in her chest as her son looked back up the stairs, his mind already working. “I think I know just the thing.”



***



Agatha came upstairs to grab a glass of water, when she found Nicky bouncing around his grandmother. “I just can’t wait to go to confession today, Grandma! There’s so much sin in the world and my little heart just wants to be good. I hope god listens to my apologies.” He stuck out his bottom lip for good measure. 

 

Evanora patted his cheek as if he was the son of god himself. “My child, you make me so proud. Of course we can go at once, just know it takes time to confess properly.”

 

Agatha almost snorted at her son’s faked emotion, he was good. “Grandma, we can be there all night if we have to, I just want to learn to do it right.” He grabbed her hand and they began to walk towards the front of the house. Agatha watched them go in awe of her son’s manipulation tactics. 

 

“Nicolas, where are you off to?” She tried to sound nonchalant. 

 

He grabbed his coat and pulled it on as he took a steading breath. “To clean my soul, Momma. I will pray for you too while we are there. I hope one day the devil leaves us alone. Right, Grandma?”

 

Evanora held his hand and grabbed her keys scooting them out the door. “You are most certainly a child of god my boy, let us go to the house of the lord.”

 

Agatha was left with her mouth hanging open as the door rattled from the slam.

 

She shook her head, her son had surely gotten the acting gene from her, she looked back towards the basement. She wouldn’t have all day. Confession couldn’t take more than an hour or two. She grabbed a glass of water and hustled to the basement. Her closet seemed like the logical place for sound quality. She read the script over and over again, she set up her laptop to record and spent some time work shopping the different ways she could say the lines. She made up her own story in her head for the character as well. She didn’t know the relationship between the two women, but in her head, the scene was heavily charged with sexual chemistry.

 

She cleared her throat and began saying the lines out loud. Imaging Rio on the other end of her harsh planned out words. She delivered the lines until they felt natural and felt like hers. Then she actually recorded. She did three takes and sent the files to Rio, closing her computer down after.

 

Her blood pumping as the creative bug bit her. She had missed this rush, she loved school and all the classes she had to take, the actors and writers she had learned from. She just wasn’t sure it was worth the debt it left her in.

 

She looked at herself in her bathroom mirror as she tried to ignore the lines that had begun to crease her face. She wished Rio would appear and tell her how beautiful she was, because she didn’t believe the sentiment right now. She reached for her flimsy makeup bag and grabbed a deep red lipstick and drew on her lips. Her eyes flashing in recognition as she felt a surge at dressing up, even just her face.

 

She took her eyeliner and drew on dark lines, Her blue eyes popping with the stark contrast. She rubbed at her forehead, trying to relax the tension there that was making the lines look more prominent than they really were.

 

She reached for her phone and took a few photos of her face, her camera painting images she couldn’t see in the mirror. The woman on her phone looked striking, she wondered if that was how Rio saw her. An illusion of herself. Before she could think better of it, she sent the photos off to Rio as well – and watched as Rio read her messages.




***

 

Rio turned her phone back on hours later. A few pings caused her to raise her eyebrows. Agatha had gotten back to her. Three audio files, and three video files sat in her inbox. She paused what she was about to do, and clicked play on the first video. Agatha was hiding in a closet.

 

She was nervous, but quickly transformed her face and her voice into whoever she was trying to be. Rio was impressed at the switch. She watched as Agatha had guessed right, that the scene was Sapphic in nature. Her lines appeared to drip with tension and frustration. Rio lost herself to the scene and was left blinking as it ended. She shook her head to wake herself up and she watched the next clip, with a similar effect, but it was the last one that broke her heart. The way Agatha’s eye’s bored into the camera, made Rio want to rip out her own heart.

 

She downloaded the files and sent them to Lilia, another ping came through. Agatha had sent her photos. She tilted her head, were these comp shots? They were clearly her in the mirror but she looked amazing. Rio sent those too. Manifesting that Agatha would impress Sharon and the Writer.

 

And she saved the photos for later.

Chapter 17 - Chemistry Read

Chapter Summary

They get their Chemistry read for the show.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

CHAPTER 17 - Chemistry 

 

Agatha tried to pay attention as Nicky explained to her how confession worked as they sat on the couch in the living room. Agatha combing through his hair with her fingers, praying for the day it was long again. 

 

Nicky’s eyes dropped back towards where his grandmother was cooking as his voice got quiet. “How was the interview, Momma?”

 

Agatha let the couch hold her up as she shrugged, “Who knows.” But she leaned forward and kissed Nicky on the head. “Thank you for helping me. We… have a chance.”

 

Nicky beamed, whispering. “Anytime, Momma. I’m always by your side.”

 

Agatha ruffled Nicky’s hair as her boy laughed. Evanora appeared in the doorway. “Dinner is almost ready. Nicolas, could you please set the table so we can pray?”

 

Nicky bounded from the couch. “Okay!” Agatha was left shaking her head and covering up her smile at her child’s antics.

 

Evanora gave her a hard stare. “You would do well to learn from the boy. He might be able to help you, if anyone can. You should pay attention.”

 

Agatha raised an eyebrow. “I was listening to him, Mother.”

 

Evenora turned her back on her and Agatha groaned quietly. She wasn’t sure how long she was going to make it if she didn’t get out of this house some day soon. Just as she was about to go help her son with the table, her phone rang. She quickly took the route to the basement, locking her door before hiding in the bathroom.

 

“Rio?”

 

The woman on the other end sounded thrilled she had picked up. “Agatha, I’m glad I caught you.”

 

She tapped her nervous fingers on her sink. “I take it you received my files the other day? Are we… done?”

 

Rio faltered. “Done?”

 

Agatha turned and sat on the sink. “Yeah… with whatever reason you needed me to do this.”

 

Rio sighed. “I thought you would be good for the role, that’s why I did this.”

Agatha drummed her fingers harder on the porcelain. “Well, I did it, so it’s time we moved on with our lives.”

 

Rio snorted. “Are you breaking up with me?”

 

Agatha’s eyes flew open. “What? We’re not…”

 

Rio huffed. “I mean it’s not like you’re my girlfriend or anything, but I had thought we were… seeing each other.” Rio sniffed a bit. “So… you’re seeing someone else, then? That was quick…” her voice hardened. 

 

Agatha blanched. “I’m not talking to anyone.”

 

Rio snorted. “What do you call what we did?”

 

Agatha shook her head. “You’ve got to be kidding me. You’re the one that wanted an NDA, it never happened, remember?”

 

Rio’s voice was raw. “I never said that.”

 

Agatha leaned her head back against the mirror. “Rio… this is never going to go anywhere…”

 

Rio tried to clear her throat but did a poor job of it. “Understood.”

 

Agatha pressed at her chest, why did she feel like she was having a heart attack. 

“Rio, just… stick to reality.”

 

Rio couldn’t contain herself anymore she blurted out her news. “They want a chemistry read.”

 

Agatha was silent, then her voice was barely audible as she responded. “They…”

 

Rio huffed, she said it slower. “They… want… a… chemistry read.”

 

Agatha gulped. “But I just broke up with you.”

 

Rio snorted. “So, we were a thing. I figured.”

 

Agatha rubbed at her forehead. “Why are you telling me this?”

 

Rio didn’t hesitate. “Because I want you to get the job, idiot.”

 

Agatha’s mouth opened in shock. “Well… who am I reading with?” She bit her lip and quickly noticed that she tasted metal.

 

“Me.” Rio’s voice was steady once more.

 

Agatha clicked her tongue. “Ah.” Her phone started to ring with a face call and she hesitated before accepting it. Rio’s splotchy face coming through. Okay, now Agatha felt worse. 

 

“We need to do it soon. Shouldn’t be too hard.”

 

Agatha’s eyes darted away from the screen. “I would need to have Nicky get my mom out of the house or… wait until she goes to sleep.”

 

Rio shrugged. “I don’t have any plans tonight.”

 

Agatha jumped as she heard her mother bang on her door. She cursed. “Fuck. Rio, I… I have to go.”

 

Dark eyes rounded. “Will--Will I hear from you tonight?”

 

Agatha looked back at Rio’s face before she decided, nodding. “Yes, I’ll… message you when the coast is clear.”

 

***

 

Agatha sat up with Nicky playing cards in the living room. Evanora had just disappeared to her room for the night. Agatha’s eyes were glued on the hall for so long that Nicky took notice.

 

“What’s the mission?”

 

Agatha shifted. “Nothing.” She placed her next card on the pile, indicating Nicky. She didn’t know why but she wanted Rio to have to wait on her, like she had needed to wait to hear that Rio had gotten home safe. She had been worried sick.

 

Nicky rolled his eyes. “Is this about… Rio?”

 

Agatha’s eyes flicked up to meet his. “Why do you think this is about her?”

 

He rolled onto his side on the floor, looking at his cards above his head. “Cause, you get moody when you think about her.” Nicky lowered his cards. “Are you in love?”

 

Agatha snorted, throwing a card at her son. “No.”

 

Nicky giggled, shaking his head so his hair was less in his eyes. “She’s pretty cool. I like her.”

 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “You like her because she buys you things.”

 

Nicky glared. “I like her because she helped me feel better.” He grumbled. “I worked hard for the iPad so I could talk to you when you leave. You didn’t want me stealing your laptop. Remember?”

 

Agatha looked back at her cards, releasing a breath, she pondered what she could tell her son. “Rio is helping me look for a job.”

 

Nicky’s voice brightened. “Cool!” He tilted his head. “Wait, where does she live? Chicago?”

 

Agatha shrugged. “Somewhere further.” She tapped the pile for Nicky to place another card. The kid rolled his eyes. 

 

“Okay…. So are we moving?”

 

Agatha sighed and set her cards down. “I don’t know anything yet, Nicky. She’s just a friend and while she’s been very kind to us… it doesn't mean we can trust her.”

 

Nicky let his shoulders drop. His voice was hesitant as he tried to reach out. “Momma?” Agatha hummed and he continued. “She’s not Mommy. She wouldn’t hurt you like that.”

 

Blue eyes looked for something in Nicky’s brown ones. “Nicky…” her voice cracked and her son continued.

 

“She’s your friend. She wants to help you, just… let her.”

 

Agatha pressed at her temples – if only it were that simple.

 

***

 

Nicky had gone to bed and promised not to interrupt her call with Rio. Agatha grabbed her laptop and moved to her closet, hopeful that the battery would hold for at least a while. She texted Rio and a moment later was sent a link. She followed it on her computer and saw Rio’s face appear on the screen, sitting in what looked like her kitchen.

 

“Hey.” Agatha rolled her shoulders.

 

Rio’s eyes roamed all over her screen. “It’s good to see you again.” 

 

Agatha sat with her back against a dresser, “Should we get going?”

 

Rio nodded. “I know my lines.” She tapped her head. “Got that photographic memory – remember?”

 

Agatha snorted, shifting to try and get comfortable on the concrete floor. “That must be nice.”

 

Rio nodded, looking a bit sad. “It can be.” 

 

Agatha noticed the uncomfortable energy that crackled between them. “Rio… earlier….”

 

The other woman cleared her throat. “Let’s just get to the reading.” Effectively cutting her off.

 

“As you picked up on, this is a Sapphic scene. My guess is that these two are exes, this scene seems charged with a past.”

 

Agatha tried to smile. “Well, I wasn’t aware we were preparing for a role that weekend.” Her smile dropped as Rio leaned her head on her hand, her voice quiet. “We weren’t.”

 

Agatha’s fingers navigated to her keyboard as she found the lines. “So how do we do this?”

 

Rio was stuck looking at her phone. “We'll read it together a couple times, then record.” She looked up. “Ready?”

 

Agatha nodded, she took her hair out of her ponytail and let it fall, tucking one side behind an ear. Launching right in. “What is it that you want?” Her eyes lifted, her voice held such devastation and desperation. She swallowed hard. “I came when you called.”

 

Rio let her eyes linger on the phone before her, her eyes tried to lift but failed to rise. Eventually they lifted, “I needed you.” Her voice held a bit of whine to it.

 

Agatha felt the now familiar throbbing in her chest and she pressed down over her heart, hard. “It won’t make a difference.” Her voice took on a quality like she was trying to hold back waves of emotions. “I can’t forgive you for…” her voice cut off as she gasped, her breath coming quickly. “You didn’t need to…”

 

Rio lifted her chin. “Yes. I did.”

 

Agatha looked away. “It doesn’t matter anymore. This power… it’s running out.”

 

Rio watched her carefully, her eyes wandering about her face presumably. “You will die if you don’t stop…”

 

Agatha screamed, to hell with her mother waking up. “Then I do! Who cares!”

 

Rio sat back in her seat, taken aback. “I just…” she shook her head. “I do.”

 

Agatha snarled. “Do?”

 

Rio’s eyes lifted clearly missing making eye contact. “Care.”

 

Agatha’s eyes watched as Rio didn’t move. Blue eyes worried after her. She was about to ask if she was alright, she lifted her hand ready to reach out – when she noticed the blinking red light. When had Rio hit record?

 

Dark eyes lifted defiantly. “In the end – I always did.”

 

Rio licked her lips. “Scene.” The red light stopped. The screen faded to black. The video call telling Agatha that the meeting had ended and a recording was being created.

 

Agatha was left with her heart racing. Desperately wanting to reach out to Rio and talk to her, but she was too much of a coward and slipped under her covers and closed her eyes, trying to forget the broken way Rio had looked at her and the realization that it wasn’t just about the character she was playing.

Chapter 18

Chapter Summary

This is the event that gets Agatha out and talking to Rio.

CHAPTER 18

 

Agatha felt Rio’s absence. She opened her phone multiple times a day just to see if she had missed anything from the woman, always feeling more disappointed when there was nothing new. She had upset Rio and the woman had still done the chemistry read with her, for her benefit. She sighed as she exited her car, her eyes looking up at her mother’s white home. She wondered if she was ever getting out, a thought that kept affronting her daily since arriving back. She took off her jacket from the hardware store. She let the cold remind her that she was still living. 

 

Nicky had been very good at going undercover with grandma so that she could chase this job Rio had handed to her. She blew out a breath, it would be a miracle if she landed the role. She watched as Nicky waved at her from the window, her chest warming as she waved back. She moved towards the house and tried not to let her steps falter as her mother appeared in the front hall for her arrival.

 

“Hey, Mom.” She closed the door and hung up her coat. “It was a cold one today.”

 

Evanora muttered a bible verse under her breath and Agatha toed off her shoes. Trying to avoid a confrontation. Sticking to her child was always a safer topic. “Nicky’s been busy this week.”

 

Her mother lifted her chin up, as if gloating about the wonderful job she was doing with the boy. “Yes, he’s being confirmed as a member of the church soon.”

 

Agatha nodded as she removed her scarf. “Ah. I see.” She of course didn’t approve of Nicky’s adventure into religion, but they did need a roof over their heads, so what was she going to do but stay silent on the matter? 

 

As she moved past her mother, she threw practiced words over her shoulder. “I’m going to take a quick shower, then I’ll be up to help with dinner.”

 

Evanora quickly jumped in. “I left you something on your bed. Don’t… rush back.” She left without looking at her again and Agatha knew something was off. She knew it wasn’t going to be something kind, but she figured she could just ignore whatever it was. As she opened her door she felt the breath leave her lungs. Something shiny sat on her bed with a note. She closed her door and locked it. What was her mother playing at?

 

A small revolver sat on top of her sheets, a note to the right. Her fingers clenched into a fist, not wanting to know at first what her mother was implying. She shook her head and went to shower, her mind not once leaving the weapon sitting idly by in her room. She washed her hair and then poured the soap into her hands, a memory coming up of another time when her wife would join her. She shifted, trying to get away from the memory. “No.” She turned and no one was there. Her hand coming up to her chest. She turned the water hot so that it would burn her. When she couldn’t stand the heat any longer, she made it cold. So cold she was shivering in seconds. 

 

She forgot to rinse her hair and stepped from the shower, letting it run, a towel wrapping around her body. She let her feet carry her back to her bed, not bothering to turn on the space heater though she was freezing. She plopped down and let her fingers reach for the note. No doubt it would be something horrible. She felt ill the moment she started to read.

 

Agatha, Nicky is finally with god now. Let him have the life he deserves so that one day he will go to heaven. He really deserves so much better than you. I had hoped you would have chosen your way out sooner, but I must ask you to please do what is best for the boy. 

 

The gun has a single bullet. I can keep him busy tonight. May God have mercy on your soul.

 

Agatha picked up the gun. She moved it to the top of her dresser, after a careful inspection there was only one bullet. She removed it and shook her head. She didn’t want to leave Nicky… did she? She moved to her phone calling the only person she had. 

 

She moved to the opposite side of the room and hid herself between her nightstand and the wall. “Please… pick up… please…” Her mantra got her past the first couple rings when a voice came over the line.

 

“Agatha?”

 

She tried to keep breathing. “Hey… I’m sorry to be calling…” her ears took in the sounds of people and music. She was trying to come back to reality, but her mind wasn’t right. “Where… Where are you?”

 

Rio sighed. “Out. There’s a new club in LA and I’m… giving it a go.” Agatha felt the tightness in her tone. Maybe Rio wouldn’t miss her either. “Did you… need something?”

 

Agatha gasped, trying to mask her upset. “No… no. I–I’m sorry I bothered you.” She heard Rio cut her off not even a second later. 

 

“Let me find somewhere to talk.”

 

Agatha gripped the phone tightly as she pulled her knees to her chest. All she had to do was keep breathing, that was all. She wasn’t alone with her thoughts or her mother’s words, Rio was here with her now. 

 

Suddenly the phone went quiet and for a brief moment she panicked that Rio had let her go.

 

Rio’s voice was hesitant but it was there. “So… what is going on?”

 

Agatha found it hard to speak to her for the first time. Her mind was yelling at her for bothering the important woman. “I’m probably overreacting.” 

 

She heard Rio try again as if the woman was sensing her desperation to hang on. “It’s just me. You can talk to me.” She tried to lighten the mood. “We’re still friends, right?”

 

Agatha groaned, becoming more aware of herself by the moment. Why had she called Rio? “Are we?”

 

Rio came down the line, her voice firm. “Yes.”

 

Agatha smiled. “Okay.” She let one leg stretch out away from her, loosening her grip. “My mother… has requested… that I leave this plane of existence.”

 

Rio’s gasp was a crack in Agatha’s soul, “That’s not the worst part.” She chuckled sadly. “She would like me to do it tonight… with the … gift she left me.”

 

Rio’s voice was low. “Get Nicky, and get out. Now.” Her voice, deadly. 

 

Agatha’s body froze at her tone, she had never heard her like that in real life, maybe in a movie once. She tried to reason with her, “Rio…”

 

Rio boomed down the line. “Agatha. Get the fuck out of there!”

 

Agatha’s eyes started to burn as she tried to calm the woman on the other end of the phone. “I don’t… have anywhere to go…” she was cut off.

 

Rio growled. “I don’t care. I’ll drag you out of that house if I have to, myself.”

 

Agatha bit her lip. “I don’t…” but Rio didn’t let her finish.

 

“You’re leaving. I’ll get you a room. Matter of fact, you need to be out here in case the job comes through.”

 

Agatha shook. “But what if it doesn't?”

 

Rio made an effort to breathe, which seemed like it took a monumental effort. “There will be other roles, you’re good. Like really good, you have a gift. Don’t waste it.” 

 

All Agatha heard in the quiet room were her own soft breaths. Rio’s voice appeared once more, begging her. 

 

“Come to LA.”

 

Agatha laughed lightly. “I don’t have money, remember?” Her head lay on her knee.

 

Rio wasn’t listening to excuses anymore, she was fed up. “You and Nicky will stay with me. Just… get to a hotel close to Chicago tonight and I will do the rest.”

 

Agatha felt her mouth go dry. “Rio, I can’t keep taking from you…”

 

Rio’s voice quieted down, as if she realized that if she didn’t do this right that Agatha might not make it past tonight at all. “You’re not taking, honey. I can give you whatever I want. And what I want to give you, is a way out of that hell hole.” She blew out a breath. “If you don’t leave tonight, I’m flying out.”

 

Agatha looked about the room. “Where… where do I go?” Her mind was racing so fast she couldn’t think. She needed help. What was the next step?

 

Rio was on the move, voices and sounds filling the phone again. 

 

Agatha whimpered. “Rio… where are you going?” Suddenly the sounds changed to cars honking.

 

“Home, I need to get you out of there. Just… go find a hotel and I’ll give my card over the phone or something. I’ll book you guys flights for the morning as soon as I get home.”

 

Blue eyes looked about the room fearful of the future, her eyes locating the gun. “Rio… what do I tell… her?”

 

Rio’s voice was deadly. “I don’t give a fuck what you say to her. Tell her you got the role and have to be there by morning. Or tell her to go fuck herself. Just get out of there or you will see how fucking crazy I can be.”

 

She stood slowly. “I… will get dressed, grab my things.” She moved to tell Rio she would call her when the woman’s voice was firm.

 

“Don’t you dare hang up. Keep me on the line.”

 

Agatha placed her on speaker as she looked around and started to gather her few items, throwing them in her suitcase with abandon. She grabbed her phone and her laptop and moved upstairs quickly. Nicky sat at the kitchen counter making cookies when he looked up and saw her, his face falling.

 

She stood tall and lowered her voice. “Nicky. Grab your things.”

 

The boy opened his mouth to ask, then thought better of it. He flew up the stairs, drawers banging as he rushed.

 

Evanora stood at the counter glowering. “Agatha, think about what you are doing.”

 

Her voice was firm, dropping into her skills she learned in college. “I got the job. We have to be there by morning.” Rio’s lies lingering at the front of her mind. Her head tried and failed to not see the gun in her mind’s eye as she looked away. 

 

Evanora gasped. “You’re not taking Nicolas!” 

 

Agatha laughed, practically cackled. “Like hell he is staying with you!” She heard as Nicky dropped his suitcase down the stairs, frantically rushing to get back to his mother. 

 

“Sorry!” Nicky said. 

 

Agatha pointed at the door. “Get your coat, get in the car.”

 

Nicky nodded and moved quickly, pulling his suitcase along.

 

Agatha turned to follow him out, grabbing her bags, when Evanora came bursting after her. “What will you do Agatha? You think this friend could actually love you? Your wife didn’t even love you! No one ever could!”

 

Agatha’s gaze was hard as she stepped into her mother, the older woman bumped back. “I don’t need anyone to love me mother, you taught me that.” She looked her mother up and down as she sneered. “I’ll see you in hell.”

 

And just like that, she left her mother’s house for the last time.

Chapter Summary

The hotel is quick then the big update :) and their reunited <3 enjoy and if you do please subscribe and leave a comment with your thoughts :))

CHAPTER 19

Agatha was exhausted as she arrived at the hotel Rio had located for her. The night was young, but all Agatha wanted was to pass out and forget. She kept moving and going through the motions until the moment when she opened the door to their room, then she finally felt it all hit her. She didn’t want to break in front of Nicky, but her mind was done. She collapsed into a heap on the floor. Nicky’s eyes wide, he quickly called Rio.

 

The woman picked up on the first ring and tried to soothe him. “Nicky, listen to me, don’t panic. Your mother will be okay. She just needs to calm down. We just need to be here with her. Can you hold her hand for me? I know you always make things better for her.”

 

The little boy quickly grabbed his mother’s hand, holding on. “I got her.”

 

Rio slowed her voice. “Good job. I promise I’ll help you with her. Just hang on for a little bit longer buddy.” The little boy heard typing as Rio tapped on her computer. “Can you put on one of your shows for you and your mom? Can you find the wifi password for the room?”

 

Nicky’s eyes looked around before his eyes flashed in recognition. “I see the card for the wifi, I’ll get my iPad.” He let his mother’s hand go while he booted up his electronic and navigated to a show, pressing play. He crawled into his mother’s lap, pulling her arms around him, feeling her body shake. “Momma, look we're going to watch a show. Just like old times, for bed, remember? Just to settle down before sleep.”

 

His mother didn’t speak, but she tried to stop sobbing, which took effort. But eventually she was just breathing, holding him tightly, as Rio sat on the phone beside them.

 

“Nicky?”

 

The kid lifted the phone, “Yeah?”

 

“I’m going to have you and your mom do a late check out. I think you’ll both need the rest. If you can remember, tell your mother your flight is tomorrow evening. I’ll send a car to take you and your mother to O’Hare. I’ll have someone from Alice’s cafe pick up your mom’s car…” 

 

Little brown eyes stared at the phone, foregoing his show. “Okay. I think I can remember that.” He sighed as he felt his mother lean against the wall, her head dipping slightly. His voice lowered so he wouldn’t wake her. “Hey, Rio?”

 

The woman on the phone stopped typing. “Yeah?”

 

Nicky had so many questions, and he wanted to ask them all, but when he landed on what he really wanted to say, it wasn’t any of them.

 

“Thank you.”

 

Rio's voice was gentle. “You’re welcome, kid.”

 

Nicky was quiet for a while, his eyes watching the cartoon without taking it in. “Hey, Rio?” He heard a sleepy hum. “Did Momma really get the job?”

 

Rio cleared her voice. “We don’t know yet. Hopefully we will know soon. But it doesn’t matter because you are going to come stay with me for a while until your mom finds something.” After a beat Rio continued. “I have a dog… do you… like dogs? I know you had wanted a puppy…”

 

Nicky smiled. “I never got to have a dog before. Does it… know tricks?”

 

Rio’s voice lifted. “Yeah, he does. His name is Ruffland. He’s funny. I think you two will get along.”

 

Nicky looked up at his mother, scooting out of her hold to grab a pillow and the sheets from the bed, laying her down gently on the floor and covering her up before he slid in with her, propping up the iPad so he could keep watching the colors and movement.

 

“I’m excited to see you tomorrow.”

 

Rio practically smiled through the phone. “I’m excited to see you, too.”
