Chapter Summary

Agatha and Rio work through some tough things. we're getting closer to the end and I'm not sure if I want to just post book two here (cause it already has all the subscriptions and then I don't have to come up with a new name etc) or start a new work in "Series" since that didn't go well with Unfortunately Famous. Basically UF had over 40k views and high engagement but when I started posting book two this year less than 200 people have found it :( Let me know your thoughts and I'll see where I land.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

CHAPTER 36 

Agatha sat in Lilia’s backyard, on an outdoor couch in her gazebo, while Nicky, Benny, and Ruffland ran around like crazy. Lilia and Rio were in the kitchen making lunch and had shooed her away. 

 

Lilia had wanted to have a lunch meeting with the two, and Agatha had a sinking feeling it had to do with the request she had made. She tried to ignore her skin prickling as she thought about the words she had typed up, knowing that this would either go very well or not at all. She tried to refocus her attention on something else. 

 

She watched everyone play and found that she couldn’t help but smile. Nicky’s happy yells as he raced around the yard brought a lightness to her chest that she needed in the moment. Her eyes scanned the yard and she realized she hadn’t seen Rio’s dog for a few moments, her smile into a look of concern. When she looked down, she almost jumped as Ruffland lay quietly at her feet. When had he gotten there? Her eyes looked around, unsettled. She didn’t have a good track record with dogs. She had been respectful of Rio’s baby but hadn’t wanted to force anything. The dog seemed to understand that she was nervous and stayed clear of her most of the time. On the rare occasion that she needed to let the dog in or out or feed him, she did so without complaint, and Ruffland was fairly well behaved, but they didn’t really interact much.

 

She had always loved animals, but the fact that a dog had not only bitten her as a kid, but also eaten her pet rabbit, kind of had her scarred for life. Her blue eyes watched Ruff as he watched her. She slowly tried to raise her legs up onto the couch, hopeful to put a few more inches between them, when the thing stood and placed his front paws on her leg. 

 

She let out a yelp of panic, fear flooding her body at the potential of another attack. When Ruff laid his head in her lap, her heart just about leapt from her chest. Her son’s feet came thundering her way. “Ruff! No.” Agatha closed her eyes and tried not to pass out. How embarrassing would it be to faint in front of her agent? All because of a dog she currently lived with.

 

Rio’s voice cut through her mind. “Nicky, I got it.” The woman rushed over as Nicky stood by with his lip between his teeth. Rio’s hand came to rest on his shoulders. “Remember how I told you Ruff does work for me?”

 

Nicky nodded, brown eyes not leaving Agatha. 

 

Rio rubbed at his back. “He’s working for your mom right now. I’ll go make sure she’s okay. You and Benny keep playing.” The little boy did look up then, unsure if he should put the fun down and go take care of his mom, but as he looked back at Rio, he let his shoulders sag, he nodded, showing he trusted Rio with his mom, and stooped over to pick up a ball for Benny. Tentatively going back to play fetch.

 

Rio moved purposely over to her lover and dog. “Hey, you alright?”

 

Agatha’s eyes closed tight. “I didn’t think he liked me.” She tried to laugh, her voice was quiet to not startle the dog on her lap. Rio nodded, taking a seat beside Agatha. She moved Agatha’s hand to Ruff’s fur, helping her pet him. “He’s tasking for you.” Her voice was incredulous.

 

Agatha opened her eyes slowly, her voice still a whisper. She wasn’t sure why Ruff had suddenly decided to take care of her as well. Surely she had done nothing to warrant this sort of attention from him. She rarely even played fetch with him that was left up to Rio and Nicky. “I thought he was trained to task for you?”

 

Rio shook her head in surprise. “He is… he must have bonded to you as well.” Her eyes connected with Agatha’s softly. “He seems to think you’re experiencing a panic attack.”

 

Agatha chuckled softly. Her mind tried to remember what she had been worried about before Rio’s dog had shut down all other thoughts with his alert. Landing on the letter when she remembered where she was. Her heart tried to speed up again at the reminder. “He… would be right.” 

 

Rio’s hand came up and wrapped her arm around Agatha’s shoulders. “What’s wrong?”

 

Agatha shrugged, trying to breathe. She wondered if it would be less painful to just pass out and start fresh. “I asked Lilia for something, and it might have been stupid.”

 

Rio leaned over and kissed Agatha on the cheek, causing Agatha to relax into her a bit. “We all ask Lilia for insane things. She wanted to murder me when I requested the audition for you.”

 

Agatha’s hand found its own rhythm petting Rio’s dog. She did find his soft fur soothing, when he wasn’t scaring the shit out of her. “Really?”

 

Rio nodded. “We had a pretty good relationship, but the look she gave me made me wonder if she was going to drop me as a client. She didn’t, though.”

 

Agatha leaned back into Rio’s hold. Forgoing her fears of public displays of affection, she needed this. “I just…thought something could be done better.”

 

Rio cringed. “Woah, that’s a big swing. Maybe Lilia is going to kill you.”

 

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Thanks for being so supportive.” Her eyes fluttered shut.

 

Rio grabbed Agatha’s face and held her steady, coaxing her eyes to open and focus on her lover. “No matter what happens, I’ve got you. Even if you made us lose our jobs.” Rio’s head nodded resolutely. 

 

Agatha snorted. “I don’t think it went that far…”

 

Rio shrugged, biting her lip. “These executive types can be… quite sensitive.”

 

Agatha gulped as Lilia set some plates down as she arrived. She held her breath as she waited for the news. 

 

“Luckily for both of you, I have a little finesse with the presentation, and Agatha here wrote a very heartfelt letter.” Lilia smiled warmly at the woman and Agatha flushed red.

 

“I just want the project to be successful,” Agatha mumbled as she tried to disappear into her seat.

 

Lilia’s gaze was thoughtful. “You did more than that, dear.”

 

Rio eyed both of them before she grew frustrated. “Is someone going to tell me what is going on?”

 

Lilia grabbed a printed paper. “Here’s Agatha’s letter.” 

 

The older woman gasped. “Lilia! Rio, don’t read that, it's stupid.” She reached for the paper, but Rio held her back with a hand as she read. Her dark eyes scanned the page quickly. At first she didn’t move but as she finished reading she took a deep breath. Her eyes lifted to Agatha. 

 

“You wrote this… because of me.”

 

Agatha’s eyes were trapped in Rio’s gaze as she uncomfortably admitted to it. “Yeah. Yeah, I… did.”

 

Lilia cleared her throat, waiting for both eyes to land on her before speaking. “Your request was granted.”

 

Rio’s eyebrows raised. “We’re getting the readings?”

 

Lilia nodded, plopping a raspberry in her mouth. “Yes. Starting tomorrow, for every major scene.” Her eyes took in Agatha. “I underestimated you.” She looked at the brunette, apologetically. “Sharon also wants me to discuss a slight raise in your contract, should this go well. We should speak on that later. In private.”

 

Rio looked confused but didn’t push. Seeming to know it wasn’t her place.

 

Agatha snorted. “You can tell me in front of Rio. I’m sure she makes a heck of a lot more than me.”

 

Lilia sighed. “Unfortunately, for someone like Rio, this industry isn’t always… fair.”

 

Rio’s eyes faded as she understood. 

 

Agatha gripped her hand. “What does she mean?” Her eyes trying to find Rio’s as the woman before her deflated. Her eyes cast out to the hills. 

 

“What Lilia means… is I am not, making a lot more than you.” Her gaze drifted back ashamed. “How much more is Agatha making?” her voice was no longer steady.

 

Agatha’s mouth dropped open, not in shock, but in anger. “Rio, there’s no way I’m making more as an unknown…”

 

Lilia raised her hand to stop her. “Rio is making more… but not by much.”

 

Rio’s form retreated. Agatha’s body missed the warmth, luckily the dog was still on her lap. “Why would they do that? Rio’s been building her career over a decade. I’m just in one show, my first show. How is that even possible?”

 

Lilia shrugged. “Rio is a woman of color, technically. She’s Scottish and Puerto Rican. This happens with a lot of my non-white clients, Agatha. They’ll offer you more because you’re white. Also, if Rio taking this role was contingent on your involvement, they had to have you. Rio is… exotic looking, but you, you are what the industry would consider a “classic beauty” easily marketed. It’s a miracle Rio was cast as the lead.”

 

Lilia sighed. “Rio is a brilliant actor, but that doesn’t always matter.”

 

Agatha’s stomach dropped. “Well, that’s not right.”

 

Lilia shrugged, “Nothing ever is.”

 

***

 

Rio had been quiet on the drive home, Nicky and Ruff passing out the moment they got in the car then again after they had both dragged themselves in the house. Agatha waited anxiously for Rio to speak to her.

 

Dark eyes avoided her. “Agatha, this isn’t about you, please don’t make it something it’s not. I’m not mad. I’m frustrated by the situation.”

 

Agatha wrung her hands. “Just tell me how to make it right. How do I fix this?”

 

Rio sighed, finally looking at her. “You can’t. I just was dealt the cards I was and that’s the end of it. I still make a good living. I can afford a house, healthcare, and investments. I just… can’t pay people to take me more seriously.”

 

Agatha grabbed her arm. “This… this show is going to make an impact. People will be looking at you for their next projects…”

 

Rio smiled sadly. “They’ll be looking at you, too. She raised her hands to map it out in the air. “Agatha Harkness, breakout star.”

 

Agatha shrunk under the backhanded compliment, and Rio dropped her hands. “Ignore me, I’m being an ass.”

 

Agatha shook her head. “You’re really not.”

 

Rio sighed. She moved forward and wrapped Agatha in her arms. “It means a lot to me that you would want to make things right.” 

 

Agatha gripped her back harder. “I’ll give you whatever amount you think is fair.”

 

Rio shook her head. “Just use it to buy the kids a bigger yard when the time is right.”

 

Agatha leaned back, her head tilted in question. Rio rolled her eyes. “I mean ya know, if we stay together and want to look for something bigger.” 

 

Agatha’s mouth parted slightly. “Are you talking about if we… get married or…” She must be misunderstanding. Rio had never once mentioned a desire to get married, but once the question was out of Agatha’s mouth, Rio’s eyes searched her pale face.

 

“Yeah… I was.” Her eyes blinked in shock that Agatha made the leap. She took Agatha’s hand. “Did you… not want to get married again?”

 

Agatha’s mouth dropped. “I…I don’t think I’m ready.” She cringed. That was the response she was going with? Hadn’t she been worried about how temporary everything could be? If they were married it would be a little harder for Rio to just walk away. Why was she self sabotaging at a time like this?

 

Rio snorted. “Well, I wasn’t asking you this moment.” She shook her head, a smile returning. “But… is that something that might be possible?” Her eyes were hopeful and that feeling, of being wanted more permanently, made Agatha uncomfortable. Because what if things went wrong?

 

She crossed her arms. “I’m really not sure.”

 

Rio nodded her understanding. “We wouldn’t have to, you know? But I would like some claim on you, before we go off to our next projects and some other woman decides to shoot her shot with you between takes.”

 

Agatha laughed. “Like anyone would even be interested.”

 

Rio’s smile fell. “You really don’t know how beautiful you are, do you?” She felt brown eyes dark to her lips before taking in the rest of her face. 

 

Agatha’s skin crawled, she hadn’t ever been one to receive compliments well. They had been so rare in her life that when she did get them, she didn’t believe them. 

 

Rio sighed. “Evanora did a number on you.” She reached up and ran her hand through dark chocolate hair. “I love your hair, I think it’s the perfect color.” Rio bit her cheek. “And your eyes, it’s rare to see that color blue.”

 

Agatha’s eyes fell to the ground. “Oh, come on, there are about a hundred girls within a mile of here that are far superior to me.” 

 

Rio shook her head. “Not one of them is as beautiful as you. Inside or out.” She leaned forward and kissed Agatha sweetly, not escalating things at all. She patted her on the cheek. “I’m locking this down. If we can’t get married, how about tattoos?”

 

Agatha shrugged a small smile gracing her face. “Aren't tattoos cursed?”

 

Rio smiled. “Only if I get your name. I’ve got a few ideas that shouldn’t condemn us.”

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 37

Chapter Summary

This chapter has a lot of feels. Nicky comes out to her mom :)

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

CHAPTER 37 - COMING OUT

Agatha had made a cup of coffee and settled into the couch to review her next script. She donned her glasses before taking a sip of her drink as she waited for Rio to join her, which took all of only a few minutes before the raven-haired woman came bounding in. Leaning in to take a sip of Agatha’s coffee before Agatha snorted.

 

“Did you want me to make you one?” The brunette raised an eyebrow at her partner in challenge. 

 

Rio frowned. “Is it not okay if I share?” She licked her lips as she set the cup down and tried to make her excuses. “I just really like how you make yours… and I don’t think I want a full cup but, if that would be easier, I can go make…” Her voice trailed off as Agatha picked up the mug and pressed it back into Rio’s hands. 

 

“It’s fine.” She watched Rio blush as she took a sip before handing it to Agatha for her to take a turn. Blue eyes rolled. She hadn’t shared a lot in her life, but she found that she didn’t mind sharing now, as long as the person she was sharing with – was Rio.  “For the record,” She kept her voice quiet. “I don’t mind sharing with you.” She felt her skin warm at the admission. Seeing Rio’s bright smile as her lover got comfortable on the couch eased her embarrassment, the awkwardness dissipated.

 

Agatha and Rio had been quietly reading their scripts for a while, both marking up the pages and working out different inflection options, slightly altering the end feeling of their performance.

 

Rio tapped Agatha and showed her her notes, Agatha hummed, considering the options before she circled one. She was becoming more confident in making decisions regarding her work, and it helped her confidence grow that Rio seemed to not only want her opinion, but value it.

 

Rio smiled at her suggestion and nodded her agreement as she continued working silently. Agatha’s eyes couldn’t help straying to the woman beside her, the one who chewed on the end of her pen as she tilted her head at the paper, lost in thought. 

 

Agatha was once again hit with a deep feeling in her chest when she looked at this woman. She wondered if she would always find Rio this adorable. She tried to shake herself awake from those thoughts and decided she needed to get herself to focus back on her work before her mind took a turn for the worse. 

 

As they continued to brainstorm, Nicky arrived in the living room, standing before them. Both sets of eyes lifting up at the same time. 

 

“Hey, Momma, can I talk to you?” Nicky tucked a fallen piece of his long brunette hair behind his ear as he held his mother’s gaze. 

 

Agatha took her glasses off and set them and the script down on the coffee table. Feeling a bit confused as her son seemed on edge. She hated it when her baby was stressed and moved to try and ease the tension. “Of course, Nicky, what’s going on?” She made sure her focus was only on her kid. 

 

Nicky’s eyes went to Rio, and the woman took a moment before her eyes widened in understanding. “Oh.” Agatha cast a side-eyed glance at the woman, wondering what all that was about. 

 

Nicky nodded at Rio. “Is now a good time?” The kid indicated with a raise of their eyebrows that it was indeed a conversation Rio knew something about. 

 

The dark-haired woman turned to Agatha, placing her hand on her thigh, running her thumb back and forth slowly before turning slightly to address her. “Agatha, Nicky has something really big to discuss with you. I want you to just… take it in. You don’t need to respond right away. I know you might need some time…”

 

Agatha looked between them in alarm. Rio’s fingers took in the slight tremor coursing through her body. “What is going on?” Her words came out measured, though internally, she wasn’t calm at all. 

 

Nicky rocked on his feet. His hair was finally getting longer, and he had started to pull it back in ponytails again. He cleared his little throat and took a deep breath before he spoke. “Momma. I like my hair long.” He eased in gently. 

 

Agatha’s face furrowed. This wasn’t a secret; she remembered the tantrums every time there was a haircut. “I know, sweetheart, I like it long too.” She offered up a smile, letting her son know that she really did agree with him. 

 

Nicky smiled. “It’s dark, like you and Rio’s. I hope it gets darker. I would really like that.”

 

Agatha narrowed her gaze. “Well, I think it’s a bit early to start dying your hair; you're only six.” Making a guess about what this conversation might really be about. 

 

Nicky rolled his eyes, shaking his head. “I’m almost seven.”

 

Agatha nodded. “That’s right, only seven.” She raised a brow at her child, indicating that she was not going to be easily swayed on the subject. Nicky had the rest of his life to dye his hair and put chemicals into his scalp, he didn’t need to start this young, in her opinion. And given his age, her rules still mattered. 

 

Rio placed her hand on Agatha’s back, and her pulse jumped. What could they have to tell her that was such a big deal? Was this not about Nicky’s hair at all?

 

Nicky tried again. “So my favorite color is purple like yours, Momma. Purple and… pink.”

 

Agatha nodded; she had noticed those colors were Nicky’s preferences, that hadn’t escaped her. She had always paid close attention to what had brought Nicky joy. She was always trying to make a smile appear on her child’s little face. She hadn’t been able to make Nicky’s life perfect, but she had been able to infuse a lot of joy in his young upbringing. 

 

Nicky scratched his arm. “I wanna be a mom one day when I grow up. Just like you.” The child waited for Agatha to have some sort of reaction. 

 

Agatha inclined her head. “I am sure you will be a great parent, sweetheart. You’re very loving and kind. I am sure that if that’s what you really want, then you will make it happen. I hope you find a partner that wants the same things in life…” She noticed that her child’s brows furrowed, her pulse rising once again. 

 

Nicky blew out a breath, and Agatha trailed off. Noting that she had somehow lost the plot once more. She wished Nicky would just put her out of her misery; the attempt to finish the puzzle on her own was causing her anxiety to gnaw at her. “What is it?”

 

Nicky stood his ground. “I want to be a mom .” He enunciated the word as if its meaning was obvious. 

 

Agatha nodded, confused. Why was Nicky so upset? She had always told him that he could be whatever he wanted to be, and she had meant that. She would always fight for his happiness. Why was he suddenly acting like she had told him he couldn’t do something? “I… fully support that, sweetheart.”

 

Nicky facepalmed, looking at Rio for a little help. Rio tilted her head toward Agatha, speaking softly. “Nicky is trying to share that… Nicky has differing ideas about Nicky’s identity then uh, she was given at birth.”

 

Agatha turned to Rio, nonchalantly correcting her. “He.” 

 

Rio shook her head, continuing to rub her hand across Agatha’s back. “No, honey… not he.” Her eyes lifted. “Is that right, Nicky? I’m sorry, I know you haven’t told me pronouns yet…”

 

Agatha’s brain went blank. She wasn’t following. Nicky nodded at Rio. “I think I am ready for she. I don’t like, hate he, but I want to try it out. Ultimately, I just want to make sure I never have to look like a man, cause… ew.”

 

Agatha’s hand covered her mouth. The words used started to seep past her clueless mind. Things were starting to click into place. Her eyes looked to Rio. Brown eyes holding her steady. She felt like she was falling, her hands moving to grip the couch cushions covertly. 

 

Rio spoke slowly. “Agatha. You don’t need to say anything right now. Just tell Nicky you love… them.” Rio cringed as she tried to help Agatha transition. She chanced a quick look at Nicky, and the child’s smile let her know that the kid didn’t mind, and she smiled gratefully at that. This would be an adjustment for all of them, but one they could conquer together.

 

Agatha's mind raced with too many questions. Before she voiced any of them, Rio’s hand pressed into her. Reminding her that maybe now wasn’t the time to speak them allowed, shaking her head slightly. Agatha rubbed her hands on her legs. “Oh… okay.” Her voice was quiet as she tried to think through things, but her mind kept going blank.

 

Nicky relaxed, seeming like a weight was lifted off of her shoulders. “Cool. So I still like Nicky for my name, but I think I want to change Nicolas. Maybe Nicole or something? I’m not sure yet.”

 

Agatha’s voice rose in pitch as her surprise took over. “Oh.”

 

Rio started to massage her back as she took over. “Thank you, Nicky, you keep us updated when you decide. Is it okay with you if your mom helps you pick out a new name? Or did you want to do that on your own?”

 

Nicky beamed. “I would love mom to help me,” She turned and flashed her a smile, and that was the first time during this whole conversation that Agatha’s smile met her eyes. Being included helped. She tried to keep breathing until it was safe to fall apart, feeling as if her world had been shifted.

 

Rio smiled. “That’s very sweet, Nicky. Maybe you and your mom can work on some ideas this week, and we can trial a few for a while until you land on what you like.” 

 

Nicky nodded and turned to go. “I think I’m going to go watch my ballet show.”

 

Rio smiled. “Don’t forget we’re going to go pick up pizza in an hour.” Nicky nodded as she bounded off.

 

Agatha’s breath she had been holding escaped her the moment her child was gone. “What…”

 

Rio squeezed Agatha. “Be careful with what you say around her. But you can talk freely with me as you work through this. I know this must be… a lot to take in. Just, let’s make sure Nicky isn’t around when you work through it.”

 

Agatha’s hands came up to cover her mouth, keeping her panicked voice low. “Did I… do something wrong?”

 

Rio shook her head, taking Agatha’s hands away from her face. “Honey, you did something right if that kid feels comfortable being herself so young.”

 

Agatha shook her head. “I’m a bit… overwhelmed with all of this.” She found that her hands were shaking, her mind racing to remember every moment she had spent with her child. The memories mixed with a healthy dose of self-loathing that she hadn’t noticed herself, that she hadn’t been a better parent. 

 

Rio ran her thumbs over Agatha’s slim fingers. “That’s understandable.” She inclined her head. “If it makes you feel better, you’re her hero. She wants to grow up to be just like you.”

 

Agatha’s eyes flooded with tears. Her voice was like gravel. “Why would…. She… .” She measured the word out slowly. “Want to be anything like me?” Agatha felt her breaths come faster. She wasn’t anything to be proud of. She had only recently found a career and started a relationship that wasn’t abusive. Nicky had spent her entire life watching idly by, seeing Agatha’s examples of what not to do. Why would she want to be anything like her mom?

 

Rio’s eyes started to fill up as well. “Because you are a great mom.” Her hand moved easily through Agatha’s dark hair. 

 

Agatha leaned into Rio. “I don’t want to mess this up.” The weight of the situation was crushing her. She didn’t know how to do this, how to raise Nicky as a girl. She felt woefully unprepared.

 

Somewhere in her panic attack, Rio kissed her head. “We are going to mess this up; that’s inevitable. But we are going to try. And we will listen to her and give her all the support she needs. We’ll learn,”

 

Agatha nodded. Her voice gasped out as if someone was strangling her. “How are you so calm about all of this?” 

 

Rio shook her head, blowing out a breath. “Oh, I wasn’t when she first told me. My gods, Agatha, I've been trying so hard not to out Nicky for a while now. It’s been torture every time we talk about…” She slowed to watch herself. “Her.”

 

Agatha sighed, biting at her lip. Her eyes held onto Rio’s like they could keep her from drowning. The realization that her child had gone to Rio first wasn’t lost on her. She wondered briefly if she was jealous, but quickly realized it wasn’t Rio she was mad at, it was herself. Because if she had done better, then Nicky would have felt comfortable coming to her first, right? 

 

Agatha took a few calming breaths before continuing the conversation. “I guess… this all makes sense. If I…think about it.” She groaned. “My gods, Tori and my mother are going to have a stroke.” She pressed at her forehead as she felt a headache coming on. If things were bad with her mother and Tori before, this surely wasn’t going to help the situation. 

 

Rio laughed. “Good, let them crash out.”

 

Agatha bit her tongue. “Do I let him…” She cringed; she had already messed up. How was she going to get this together in front of Nicky when she couldn’t even do it right in front of Rio? She adjusted her word choice. “Do I let her… dress up like a girl now?”

 

Rio shrugged. “When she’s ready. She’s pretty androgynous in her style, but who knows, that may change. She’s a bit of a tomboy.”

 

Agatha nodded. “Yeah. She is.” Her chest heaved, and her hand moved to rub over her heart. “Wow, this is hard.”

 

Rio nodded. “It is. It’s even harder for Nicky.”

 

Agatha’s eyes dropped, feeling that truth hit her in the face. She bit her lip to try and tamper her emotions. “I want Nicky to be happy.” 

 

Rio pulled Agatha into a hug. “She will be.”

 

Agatha took another breath as she returned the hug. Her eyes pinched shut. Rio’s warm and sturdy presence allowed her brain to start functioning, and she voiced her first thought.  “Maybe we take…. Her… to get her nails done? She really likes her nails painted.”

 

Rio smiled. “That’s a great idea. Maybe we can even just start painting them at home? Could be a fun activity for all of us to do together.”

 

Agatha cuddled up with Rio, praying she wouldn’t point out their current position right now because she couldn’t handle the overthinking that would also cause. “I would love that.”

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 38

Chapter Summary

Jen and Agatha solve the Sext-IT mystery! Any guesses?

Easily the funniest chapter. While you wait for Good Hang with Amy Pohler and KATHRYN HAHN to drop tomorrow, why not catch up with Thirst (Trap) ?

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

CHAPTER 38 

 

The third post it note arrived in Agatha’s car that morning, on her steering wheel. She nearly screamed in frustration. How was this person getting into her car now? At her own home… well, Rio’s home. Shit .

 

She drove to work so tense her shoulders were up to her ears. When she arrived, she burst into the hair and makeup trailer like a thunderstorm. Her emotions swirling and cracking, begging for the energy to unleash itself onto someone, anyone. Jen, unfortunately for her, was sitting innocently in her chair, enjoying her coffee. Having a quiet moment before the start to her day, a quiet moment that Agatha had now shattered. 

 

Jen let her head fall back as she let out a disgruntled groan. “No. No, no.” She whined. “Why did you have to come see me first with that attitude?” She moved to stand, and as she did, Agatha’s hand slapped a group of green notes to her chest.

 

“Is this a game to you?” Agatha’s eyes were pleading with Jen. Hoping she would admit this was just her playing some prank on Agatha, just like they used to do in school; that way she could move on with her life and not need to worry that someone was lurking too close to her family. 

 

Jen set her coffee down as her hand held the notes, lifting them to her eyes. She read them slowly, her mouth dropping open in shock the more she read. Until finally her hand covered her mouth in horror. She lowered her hand as her eyes lifted. “Shit, Agatha, this is bad.”

 

Blue eyes rolled. Agatha started pacing her, hand rubbing at her lips, the skin there already running raw with her worry. “So, it’s not you.”

 

Jen shook her head slowly. “These… this is probably a fan, but nonetheless, you should go to the police. Where do you keep finding these?” Dark eyes continued to read the words transcribed on the little papers as if perhaps there might have been some clue she had missed. 

 

Agatha crossed her arms feeling ill at east. Her voice grew quieter, eyes looking around to see if there were hidden cameras she could spot. Her shoulders fell. Her eyes indicated the first location. “That chair.” Her eyes pointed to where Jen had been sitting, watching as her friend’s eyes only grew rounder. Blue eyes lifted to the door. “Another, on my trailer door.”

 

She sighed, pointing at the one Jen was now reading. “That one was on my steering wheel this morning, greeting me on my way to work.”

 

Jen’s eyebrows shot up. “ In your car?”

 

Agatha nodded as she took the notes back and read over the most recent one once more.

 

So how do you feel about back seats? ;)

 

Jen’s eyes looked up as a thought struck her. “Why didn’t we try my backseat instead of the forest floor…”

 

Agatha growled. “Jen! Not helping.” She wanted to remind Jen that they had been stupid, hormone riddled children when they had hooked up, but getting on Jen’s nerves was not the priority right now. She could work on that task later. 

 

Jen waved her off, as the severity of the situation sunk in. “Okay, okay. Let’s think. Who has access to this room… and how did they get access to this set?”

 

Agatha bit her lip. “I have no clue.” Her fingers started to twitch. 

 

Jen leaned on the chair, her hands crushing the backing. “You have to tell Rio.”

 

Blue eyes wandered about the room before they landed back on the notes. “I know. I just… don’t want to worry her.”

 

Jen’s jaw dropped. “Well, it’s better than one of these days she just finds you dead from a stalker, or hell, Agatha, what if something happens to Nicky or Rio!”

 

Agatha placed her hand on her chest, rubbing firmly. Her mind provided an unhelpful vision of Rio and Nicky all dressed in black before an image of coffins dominated her mind’s eye, and… was that Jen with snot running down her face in the corner of her vision, at the funeral? CHAPTER 39

CHAPTER 40

 

Agatha shut the passenger side door as Rio came around and grabbed her hand. Blue eyes looked around and took in their studio lot, biting her cheek subtly. Her mood instantly fell with the temperature outside of the car. “Rio, it’s cold. What are we doing here?” She had wanted to stay home and have a quiet night in, but her… she guessed girlfriend now, had mentioned that she had forgotten her favorite sweatshirt on set and that they had to go retrieve it… right this instant, before she never saw it again. Luckily, Lilia had been available to rush over and take care of Nicky.

 

Rio bit her lip, clearly nervous. “I don’t want someone to take it, Agatha. I left it on the set, you know there are so many people who come through here daily...” She pulled her along as Agatha rolled her eyes.

 

“We know most of the people.” She sighed. “I am sure someone would have grabbed it for you, noticing it was yours.”

 

Agatha followed Rio, briefly dropping her hand as her partner entered the code for the side door and they stepped into a pitch black set. Well, nearly pitch black, there were some emergency lights that glowed around the perimeter. Rio turned and placed her hands on Agatha’s shoulders. “I’ll go get it, you just wait here. We don’t need both of us breaking our ankles.” She smirked as she took off, illuminating the space before her with her phone’s flashlight.

 

Agatha shivered as she watched her go. It wasn’t much warmer in the building than outside, but at least it wasn’t wet. She looked around the familiar space, noticing the outline of the trees they filmed with frequently were ahead of her as her eyes adjusted. As the moments continued to stretch, she wondered what was taking Rio so long. She had expected a quick “got it” to ring out within the first few minutes they were here, but the set remained silent aside from the hum of the emergency lights. 

 

Maybe Rio really hadn't even left her sweatshirt on set and it was sitting at home in the laundry this whole time. She had asked her multiple times if she had checked everywhere before she had agreed to get into the car, she wondered now if she should have double checked herself. Come to think of it, she didn’t really remember the sweater that Rio had described to her, she wondered why she hadn’t seen it before. 

 

Agatha bounced on her toes as she tried to warm up. Rio had brought Agatha her green puffer jacket, but she had left it in the car, knowing that they wouldn’t be here long. She started to wonder if she should go back and get it. Her eyes shifted to the forest as the lights had just come on. Rio must have needed a bit more light for her search. Blue eyes rolled, so she had forgotten where she left her sweatshirt. Typical .

 

She let her eyes take in the flickering of purple, green, and blue lights. She tried to hold on to her frustration but the beauty that surrounded her was hard to ignore. She figured she might as well wander over through the forest and help Rio look, after all apparently this sweatshirt was important to her lover. 

 

Her hands came up to brush the trees and shrubs that packed the area. She glanced around, but Rio was nowhere in sight. “Rio? You find it?” She continued to watch her step as she moved through the foliage. A soft track of bugs and water started playing, and she smiled. This really was starting to feel magical, like she was really in an enchanted woods. She was glad production had gone for a more practical approach because it made believing where you were so much easier when you were immersed in it and could really see it all.

Nicky leaned back and looked up at her Momma. “Rio is ours now?”

Nicky threw herself towards Rio, the woman catching her easily and holding her close. “Thanks for the help, Nicks.”

CHAPTER 41 

 

Agatha sat in the backyard alone. Her hand firmly gripped her hair as her eyes couldn’t see straight. The ring on her finger felt heavy. What if she messed it all up? She had before, hadn't she? By tying herself to the wrong person? What if her mother was right and she was cursed?

 

Agatha wore a black cropped tank top that didn’t even come to the bottom of her ribs, a long black skirt with tooling that looked like the night sky in the light, covered her legs from the slight chill in the California night air. Her feet were bare but with a dark blue nail polish that Nicky had chosen and wanted the three of them to wear when they had all done their nails the day before.

 

Nicky … she was going to need to start hormone blockers soon. Agatha rubbed at her scalp. Were those better than the hormones she had let ravage her own body? She knew literally nothing about transitioning. 

 

She stood and walked further into the yard, her hand releasing her hair and her eyes looking up at the moon, surprised it was visible in the Los Angeles night sky. She sighed. Everything was moving too fast now. The end of the show, getting engaged, Nicky’s transition, her divorce. She felt like she was spinning and might fall at any moment. She walked a bit further before she found that she had to lay down, her hair sprawling out around her. She looked for stars, but they were hard to find. She did enjoy the nighttime clouds, hopefully, they were clouds and not pollution.

 

She took a deep breath and let it out. She did so again. And again. She closed her eyes, one hand on her chest the other on her stomach, she practiced her breathing. She had a plan. She had gotten dressed, she allowed her hair to air dry with a mouse that Jen had sworn worked wonders for her curls, and it really had. 

 

She had donned jewelry for the evening. She wore small golden hoop earrings. She had done her makeup, dark eyeliner with purple eyeshadow, her lips with a soft pink. She lifted her hand in front of her face and opened her eyes, a beautiful ring now sat on her hand most of the time. Well, sometimes, because at times, she was too terrified to wear it and feared she would lose it – other times, she feared it wasn’t real and found she had to keep it on to ground herself. 

 

She curled on her side and noticed that while she had been panicking, she had completely missed that Rio had joined her outside, brown eyes were wide staring up at the sky. Agatha held Rio in her sight as if the moment she looked away, Rio would finally fade, an illusion, and she would be back in her mom’s basement. Rio’s hand reached out and grabbed hers without looking, dark eyes continuing to watch the stars.

 

“You’re worried.” Rio whispered. 

 

Agatha nodded. Her voice was thick with all of the things that weighed heavily on her mind.  “What if it doesn’t last?”

 

Rio sighed. Her head turned to look at Agatha “What if it does?”

 

Agatha bit her lip. “You got your next role, didn’t you?”

 

Rio nodded. “It films in LA, my love. I’ll be home every night…”

 

Agatha swallowed. “I won’t get to see you very much.” She blew out a breath. “I know how much you work.”

 

Rio rhythmically squeezed at Agatha’s hands as she tried to reassure her. “Agatha, they’re looking at giving us a season two and the show hasn't even aired yet. Be patient, my love, this is just another pilot season.”

 

Agatha kept their hands intertwined as she came closer. Her head ducking into Rio’s shoulder. Rio wrapped an arm over Agatha’s and started to play with her hair. “Te veo.”

 

Agatha knew she did. Rio knew her too well most of the time. She only wished she knew the dark haired beauty as much. “Will you love me when I’m… older?”

 

Rio shook her head, entertained. “Baby, I’ll be older too. And of course I will.” She kissed Agatha’s dark hair. 

 

Agatha breathed in her scent, there was something about the way that Rio smelled that she found could always calm her. 

 

Rio let her relax for a while when she finally spoke. “Okay, as beautiful as this is, I don’t think either of us want to wake up in morning dew so,” As Rio moved to sit up, Agatha bolted upright.

 

“Wait.”

 

Rio sat up slower, but didn’t move to stand. Waiting. 

 

Agatha sat with her legs under her, her ankles out to one side. 

 

Rio cupped her face. “You look beautiful tonight.”

 

The brunette snorted, as if she didn’t quite believe her. “Honey, everything looks good on me.” She joked as she let her eyes drift away. 

 

Rio turned her chin back to her and locked with her gaze, nodding her head seriously as her brown eyes darted down to Agatha’s pink lips and back to crystal blue. “It does.”

 

Agatha raised her fingers nervously to her lips. “I wanted to talk to you.”

 

Rio reached out and held a pale hand, and this time it wasn’t for Agatha’s benefit. “Okay…”

 

Blue eyes looked around the yard, a glow coming from the garden lights. It wasn’t as impressive as on set, but she wasn’t really sure how to do this. Agatha let her head fall forward a bit before she lifted her eyes. “I… don’t know how…”

 

Rio’s brows furrowed. “Okay.”

 

Agatha moved to slowly cover Rio’s eyes, “Maybe if you just… there.” The other woman getting the idea and playing along. Rio sat there with her eyes closed, her body relaxed and trusting, the only indication that she was nervous was her tight grip on Agatha’s hand.

 

Agatha reached into her bra and breathed a sigh of relief that the ring was still there. She shifted onto her knees and placed it in her lap, her hands finding Rio’s face and kissing her softly. Rio gave into her instantly, melting into her, as Agatha’s hands moved swiftly.

 

Quickly taking Rio’s hand and guessing at the finger, slipping the ring on. The kiss broke the moment it slid into place. Her eyes opening, sitting back just far enough that she could see Rio’s reaction. Dark eyes opened, lowering to the ring and lingering. It was agonizing during the long moments that Agatha waited for Rio to say something.

 

The woman was stunned for quite a few heartbeats, then a smile bloomed across her face. The green and black gems contrasting nicely with the white gold. “Sweet.”

 

Agatha scoffed. “Sweet. Really?”

 

Rio shrugged. “Well, what am I supposed to say? You haven’t asked me anything yet.” She teased quietly before she leaned forward. “It’s beautiful.” Rio’s head tilted in question. “How did you…”

 

Agatha’s shoulders pulled in a little. “Lilia loaned me the money, said she would just add it to her cut. She… tried to pay for some of it, but I told her I wanted to pay for it all. She… helped me figure out how much I should spend…I made sure it had your favorite colors,”

 

Rio’s eyes started to water. “I’m going to take good care of you and Nicky. I promise.” Her voice was a bit unsteady as she fought back tears. “Shit. I didn’t think I was going to cry again.”

 

Blue eyes started to water as well, but she held the tears back. “Thank you, I know you will.”

 

Rio grabbed her suddenly and kissed her again, pouring her whole soul into the kiss with Agatha. As if she also needed confirmation that Agatha was really there and wasn’t going anywhere.

 

When they took a breath, Rio’s eyes looked towards the house. “This is so cute, but I really am getting cold, can we?”

 

Agatha nodded and she stood, extending a hand to Rio, the woman taking her hand gently. “Wow, what a gentleman.”

 

As Agatha pulled her up with a grunt, she shook her head when Rio didn’t release her hand. “Only for you, mi amor.” Rio said.


Walking back to the house hand in hand, Agatha didn’t have all of her questions answered, but she knew that her and Rio were going to be together for a long, long, long time. She hoped that one day, when it all inevitably came to an end, that Rio’s face would be the last one she would see before it all went dark.

Chapter Summary

First this Book 1 is now complete and Book 2 is started -- just click next work :). I will load Ch 2 of that one soon as well.

Thank you to everyone who came along on this journey with me. It was born of being home in December and writing an Agathario Xmas present for my wife and thinking why don't I start a story off of two interviews I've watched. I had this idea that wouldn't leave me alone that what if they met through a thirst post interview? There are many artists and talent that admit that they have become friends or dated fans over the years so it's not fantastical as it seems.

I wanted to show a theater kid that had lost their way in life and made an amazing comeback in their art and love. While I am a performer at heart I am in no means a theater kid. I've done plays and sang in talent show but this goes out to my friends and family and people that are true theater kids and actors and couldn't imagine doing anything else. I hope you gained a bit more empathy for talent and those that work in the industry and remember that under it all -- they're real people. <3 see you over on Book 2 angst WITH A HAPPY ENDING. It will be a ride hold on.

CHAPTER 42 The Premier

They had done another practice shoot with Alice to simulate the photos taken on the red carpet, but Rio knew that the practice would pale in comparison to the chaos and the people that would be shouting your name to get a photo for their publication. 

 

There would be videos taken and screaming fans that wanted a photo or autograph. She watched as they pulled up, the press for their show had generated a larger crowd than she had thought imaginable. Her skin tingled under the anticipation, wishing she could take Agatha far away from here. 

 

In her mind she sighed, this was Agatha’s big night, just as much as hers. Her love deserved this. Rio had seen the way they marketed the show, and although Rio was the main character, somehow, Agatha got more promo shots displayed and was larger on the billboards, dwarfing her. She loved her partner, but wished things were different. People would definitely be a bit confused when they tuned in and the story focused on Rio, but she knew the key to success was doing whatever it took to get people to watch. What was important was that they got a second season and she got more time to craft worlds with her fiancé.

 

How weird that was still, her fiancé . Rio had secretly always hoped she would find someone, but never thought it would actually happen. Agatha had been a whim, an impulse she couldn’t stop. There was just something about her that drew Rio in and kept her utterly obsessed. She reached out to adjust her lover’s hair and Agatha blushed. 

 

“I’m sorry, I’m such a mess.” Agatha muttered. 

 

Rio’s eyes shifted behind her. “Just smile and wave. Take a few photos if you are ready to, and don’t let them see you sweat.” She leaned forward and kissed Agatha hard as the driver moved around the car to open the door. 

 

Agatha’s eyes were wide as she chased Rio’s retreating lips a moment later. “You get the rest when we get inside… we’ll find somewhere.” Her eyes looked up at the man and nodded before looking back at Agatha… “Now go.”

 

Agatha turned as the door opened before her, she panicked and turned back, showing her back to the crowd. “Wait, do we tell people that we’re… Do I keep this on?” She held up her hand indicating her ring. 

 

Rio’s smile was bright. “Well, I didn’t buy it for you to remain your dirty secret.” She nodded, winking. “Go let them know you're taken.”

 

Agatha beamed and turned to exit the car, not taking the man’s hand as she did, and surprising Rio when she turned back and took Ro’s hand and helped her from the car. Rio surprised herself by keeping their hands together as they walked the carpet. She led the way, taking photos and pulling Agatha with her to take photos with a few fans, many wanting photos with both women together. 

 

They took turns doing their single shots in front of the cameras and Rio waited for Agatha with an outstretched hand when she was done. “Good job.” She pulled her inside and towards where the bathrooms were hidden in the back of the house. She had luckily been to this venue before. Rio’s voice lowered. “Now you get your reward.”

Agatha’s eyes were wide.

Both women started on a jumbled, but passionate, review of the artistry of the script. Both admiring how raw and deep with emotion the piece was able to go. Sharon’s face couldn’t have been happier. She was practically bouncing on her feet when she looked at Agatha. “The table reads did just the trick, Harkness! I’ve got my eye on you for producing one day. I’m going to need talent like that in my corner for future projects.” She smiled.

 

“That would be wonderful… but honestly, Rio is the one that gave me the idea. She really has the creative eye for process.” Agatha offered softly. 

 

Rio’s eyes widened as Agatha gave her credit. Sharon turned her gaze to the star of her show. “Well, Miss Vidal, it seems we have some work ahead of ourselves for you as well. You did a great job with the protagonist. I must say, I see why Agatha sings your praises. Ash said you adjusted a few things with the choreo and I must say, I loved how personal and intimate it felt.” Her eyes lingered on Rio’s ring finger where it was wrapped around Agatha’s waist.

 

“Are we just friends, or do I spy something on that finger, Miss Vidal?” Her blue eyes casting a not so sneaky glance at Agatha’s hand and smirking when she saw a ring on her finger as well. A purple amethyst surrounded by small diamonds sparkling away as it caught the lighting. 

 

Rio shrugged. “I had to have her.”

 

Sharon nodded. “Ah, and how did we meet? I assume you already knew her if you were ready to barter for her involvement in this project?” She addressed Rio but then her eyes also slid to Agatha. 

 

***

 

Agatha wasn’t sure what she was allowed to say, so she looked at Rio, hopeful that she would take the lead and the woman did.

 

“It was an interview I did actually. I saw Agatha and I just, had to know more.” She blushed lightly.

 

Sharon patted Rio’s shoulder. “You have an eye for talent indeed, my dear.” The lights flickered and they assumed Sharon Davis would take her seat, but she turned back to them excitedly. 

 

“I’m not really telling anyone this, but… I wrote this piece.”

 

Both women’s jaws hit the floor. Rio stumbled. “ You… you’re serious?”

 

Sharon smirked and nodded. “I drew from my own experiences with women, and from my dear husband and his experience with men.” She looked behind her as she saw the MC wave her over. “Oh drat, I have to go give a little speech. I will be chatting with you two later.” She pointed at them. “You better both be available for a second season, I heard whispers in the wind that I am going to finance it.” She shrugged. “Just don’t get too busy.” As she turned to leave, Rio turned and practically jumped into Agatha’s arms. 

 

“Baby! Oh my gods, did we just get another job?” 

 

Agatha smiled, knowing that while another credit to her body of work would be great, she had already won by securing Rio in her future. “I’m thrilled, honey.”

 

Rio pulled back, a smile permanently on her face as she sat to watch the first episode, her hand playing with Agatha’s the whole time. As the lights dimmed, Rio’s face came on screen, larger than life, and Agatha was projected back to the same feeling she got every time this woman’s face came on screen. 

 

She would devote the rest of her life so that this woman knew how special and precious she was. She couldn’t believe that Rio had pursued her , but she wasn’t going to take any of it for granted. As she sat there in the theater, with her own face coming up on screen, she tried to lose herself in the story so she wouldn’t cringe nor critique herself too hard for the choices she had made.


The flashback was steamy. Agatha was blushing and hot for the rest of the premier. Wishing desperately that they didn’t need to stop at the after party, so she could just take Rio home and undress her. But this was Rio’s night in the spotlight and she would help her shine as brightly as she could, because not only did she love her but Rio fucking deserved it.
